## Tickets {#tickets}

* ## Ticket: Phase 1: Minimal core + browse-fs recipe {#1}

      status: done
      created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
      updated: 2026-04-30 08:16:07 UTC

  Goal: single-file `browse-tui` builds and runs; full async data layer with
  Pending chains and background-update support; Python API is feature-complete
  for a recipe like `browse-fs` to wire up; CLI shim handles tsv/json input,
  shell-template actions, --python, --install/--uninstall.

  Exit criterion: `browse-fs` is usable as a daily-driver replacement for
  ranger-style file browsing.

  Spec reference: `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-browse-tui-design.md`,
  Phase 1 section.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Item dataclass and coercion (TDD) {#3}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 03:56:45 UTC

    `030-data.py` partial — Item type only.

    - Tests first in `test/unit/test_item.py`:
      - Item construction: required `id`, defaults for
        `title`/`tag`/`tag_style`/`has_children`.
      - `title` falls back to `str(id)` via `__post_init__`.
      - Arbitrary extra attrs survive (e.g., `item.size = 1234`).
      - `to_item(x)` coerces from `Item`, `str`, `tuple` (1–5 elements
        positional), and `dict`.
      - Mixed lists are coerced element-wise.
      - Unsupported types raise `TypeError`.
    - Implementation: `@dataclass` Item + `to_item(x)` helper.

    * ## Comments {#3:comments}

      * Tests written: 25 tests across 6 TestCase classes (TestItemConstruction, TestToItemFromItem, TestToItemFromStr, TestToItemFromTuple, TestToItemFromDict, TestToItemUnsupported, TestMixedListCoercion). All failing as expected (AttributeError on Item — proves tests exercise not-yet-existing code). {#3:comment:37}

      * All 25 tests passing. Implementation in src-tui/030-data.py: Item dataclass + to_item() coercion helper. Build still works (./browse-tui --version prints 0.1.0). Decisions: empty tuple raises TypeError (no id); 6+ element tuples raise TypeError (no field to land in); dict-with-extras splits known dataclass fields from extras and setattr()s the extras post-construction; ints/None/list/set raise TypeError. {#3:comment:38}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Input format parsers (tsv, json, json-array) (TDD) {#4}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 04:03:07 UTC

    Phase 1 ships tsv and json (and json-array). csv/ifs/split/match land in
    phase 2.

    - Tests first in `test/unit/test_parsers.py`:
      - tsv: simple rows, empty fields, mixed widths, CRLF tolerance.
      - json: one object per line, mixed types, malformed-line tolerance
        (skip + warn vs hard error).
      - json-array: whole stdout as one JSON array.
      - Field mapping: `--fields=id,title` maps positional columns to Item
        attrs; extra columns become arbitrary Item attrs.
      - record-sep: nl (default) and null (NUL byte).
      - has_children coercion: `1/0/true/false/yes/no/y/n/empty` →
        bool, case-insensitive.
    - Implementation in `080-cli.py` parsers section: each format is a small
      function that takes raw bytes and yields dicts.

    * ## Comments {#4:comments}

      * Tests written: 54 tests in test_parsers.py, all failing as expected (ImportError on parse_input — proving they exercise real code) {#4:comment:39}

      * All tests passing: 79 total (25 from #3 + 54 new in test_parsers.py). Build still produces working ./browse-tui binary. Round-trip parse_input -> to_item verified end-to-end. {#4:comment:40}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Visible-tree builder and scope stack (TDD) {#6}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 05:42:49 UTC

    `040-state.py` — visible-tree builder + scope_stack mechanics.

    - Tests first in `test/unit/test_visible_tree.py` and
      `test/unit/test_scope_stack.py`:
      - Build visible list from a flat `_children` dict + `expanded` set.
      - Items not in `expanded` don't expose their children.
      - Empty children list (cached `[]`) renders no children.
      - Scope: when `scope_stack` non-empty, root is the scope item.
      - Scoping preserves per-scope expanded sets via `_expanded_by_scope`.
      - Pending state (children not yet cached) yields a placeholder marker
        in the visible list.
      - Refresh invalidates cache and marks the visible-tree dirty.
    - Implementation: `visible_items()` and supporting state mutators in
      040-state.py.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Async workers, post queue, and headless mode {#7}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 05:52:08 UTC

    `040-state.py` — `_children_worker`, `_preview_worker`, main_queue,
    `Browser._headless` test mode + `start_workers/stop_workers/run_until_idle`.

    - Tests in
      `test/async_/test_workers.py`,
      `test/async_/test_post_queue.py`,
      `test/async_/test_chains.py`,
      `test/async_/test_background.py`:
      - children worker: FIFO queue, fetches in order.
      - preview worker: latest-wins single slot.
      - post queue: callable from any thread, drained on main thread.
      - Pending resolves when worker delivers result.
      - Two threads refreshing same id → both Pendings resolve (phase 1
        does not coalesce; phase 3 will).
      - `.then()` on resolved Pending fires immediately.
      - Worker error → cache `[]`, error surfaced via `error_text`,
        Pending still resolves.
      - Background `browser.refresh()` from a watcher thread reaches the
        worker.
      - `Browser._headless = True` skips terminal init.
    - Implementation: thread classes, queue mechanics, headless flag,
      `notify_wake` self-pipe wiring (the self-pipe lives in 020-terminal).

    * ## Comments {#7:comments}

      * All async tests passing: 149 total (120 baseline + 29 new). 3 consecutive runs all green, no flakiness. notify_wake stub in 020-terminal.py (Option A); _preview cache lives on State alongside _children; tests inject Item/to_item/notify_wake into _state via test/async_/_helpers.py. {#7:comment:44}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Context plus default built-in actions {#11}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 06:26:53 UTC

    `060-context.py` (Context class) and `070-actions.py` (default actions
    + custom-action dispatch).

    - Context wraps Browser; adds main-thread-only sub-flows.
      Phase-1 affordances: `refresh / cursor_to / expand / select / message /
      error / input / confirm / run_external / page / quit`.
      NO pick/insert (phase 2).
    - Default keybindings:
      `j/k`, arrow keys, `home/end`, `pgup/pgdn` for nav;
      `right/left` for expand/collapse + parent jump;
      `/` enters search; `enter` is search-next-or-default-action;
      `shift-enter` previous match; `esc/q/ctrl-c` quit;
      `ctrl-r` reload; `ctrl-l` redraw; `ctrl-p` toggle preview;
      `?/f1` help; `space` reserved for multi-select (phase 2).
    - Custom action registration via `Browser(actions=[…])` and
      `Browser.add_action()`.
    - on_enter behaviour: `print-exit` (default fzf-mode), `action:KEY`,
      `noop` (long-running mode).

    * ## Comments {#11:comments}

      * Implemented Action dataclass + dispatch in 070-actions.py and Context wrapper in 060-context.py. {#11:comment:48}

        Files modified:
        - src-tui/060-context.py: Context class, run_external/page/input/confirm sub-flows, _read_line_on_info_bar/_confirm_on_info_bar helpers
        - src-tui/070-actions.py: Action dataclass, default_actions(), build_keymap, dispatch_key, _handle_enter
        - src-tui/040-state.py: added Browser.add_action()
        - test/unit/test_actions.py: 25 tests (Action, gate, defaults, build_keymap, dispatch nav/search/enter, add_action)
        - test/unit/test_context.py: 23 tests (construction, cursor/selected/targets, pass-through, headless run_external/input/confirm)
        Tests: 192 baseline -> 240 (+48). 3x flakiness check passes. Build OK.
        Decisions:
        - Action lives in 070-actions.py (not split out) so the dispatch+definitions are colocated.
        - _read_line_on_info_bar/_confirm_on_info_bar are real implementations using the terminal layer; headless mode short-circuits to default/False so unit tests can drive deterministically. UI tests in #14 will exercise the real TTY path.
        - Did NOT defer input/confirm tests — added the headless contract tests here per spec.
        - _PAGE_ROWS=10 hardcoded (page size); ticket #13 will replace with actual layout_panes() height.
        - Custom actions override defaults via dict 'last write wins' in build_keymap.

  * ## Ticket: Task: CLI parser, --python loader, --install/--uninstall {#12}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 06:36:04 UTC

    `080-cli.py` — argument parsing + special modes.

    - All phase-1 flags from spec: data flags
      (`--children-cmd`, `--root-cmd`, `--root-id`, `--preview-cmd`),
      `--action`, `--on-enter`, `--print-format`,
      `--no-preview`, `--input` (tsv|json|json-array only in phase 1),
      `--fields`, `--record-sep`, `--title`, `--initial-scope`,
      `--command-log`, `--version`, `--help`.
    - `--python SCRIPT [args…]`: insert self into
      `sys.modules['browse_tui']`, then `runpy.run_path(SCRIPT, run_name='__main__')`.
    - `--install/--uninstall {local|user|system|env}`: copy/remove the
      running binary to/from the corresponding path; emit `sudo cp …` hint
      for `system` when not root; error for `env` if `$VIRTUAL_ENV` unset.
    - Action template execution: `bash -c CMD` with `TUI_*` env vars exported
      (TUI_ID, TUI_TITLE, TUI_TAG, TUI_TAG_STYLE, TUI_HAS_CHILDREN,
      TUI_<custom_attrs>, TUI_IDS_FILE, TUI_IDS_COUNT, TUI_TARGETS, TUI_BIN).
      `--action-timeout` defaults to 600 seconds.
    - Tests in `test/unit/test_cli.py`: arg parsing, --python self-injection
      simulated with a fake script, --install dry-run via tmpdir.

    * ## Comments {#12:comments}

      * Implemented argparser, install/uninstall (4 targets w/ sudo hint + venv-error), --python self-injection via runpy, action template runner with TUI_* env, KEY:LABEL:CMD parsing, top-level main() routing. 25 new tests in test/unit/test_cli.py; total 265 (240 baseline + 25), 3-run stable. 090-main.py now dispatches via main(). run_tui() left as NotImplementedError for #13. Action wrapper delegates to run_action_cmd (handles temp ids file + cleanup), wrapped in term_suspend/term_resume in non-headless mode. Install dry-run isolated by chdir to tmpdir + faked sys.argv[0]. {#12:comment:49}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Layer-3 UI tests (tmux fixture and phase-1 coverage) {#14}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 08:02:10 UTC

    `test/ui/fixtures/tmux.py` and `test/ui/test_*.py`.

    - `TmuxFixture`: bash-launched, `send_line/launch/send/send_bytes/`
      `capture/wait_for/wait_stable/resize`, `pane_pid`, `fg_pid` (walks
      children of bash), `signal(sig)`, `ctrl_c`, `ctrl_z`, `fg`.
    - Skip-if-no-tmux at top of `test_ui.py` modules.
    - Tests:
      - Initial render at fixed dims.
      - Down/up cursor movement; expand/collapse.
      - Search (/, then text, enter for next match).
      - Custom action invocation; verify TUI_* env vars set correctly.
      - Async loader (⧗) appears for slow children-cmd, replaced by
        content when fetch completes.
      - Background update via watcher refreshes list within 2 seconds.
      - Resize handling.
      - Ctrl-Z then `fg` round trip leaves screen identical.

    * ## Comments {#14:comments}

      * Implemented per ticket spec. Files created: test/ui/fixtures/tmux.py (fixture), test/ui/recipes/{slow_children,fs_watcher}.py, and 6 test modules: test_navigation.py (4), test_search.py (2), test_actions.py (2), test_async_ui.py (2), test_resize.py (1), test_suspend.py (1) = 12 UI tests total. Suite total: 288 tests in 6.2s, UI subset 12 tests in 3.8s. 3 back-to-back runs all green; no tmux leaks (pgrep count unchanged). Skip path verified by mocking shutil.which. {#14:comment:53}

        Production fixes uncovered while writing the tests:
        1) ctrl-z byte was a no-op: in raw mode (tty.setraw clears ISIG) the kernel does NOT translate \x1a to SIGTSTP. The terminal layer's _handle_sigtstp existed but was never invoked from the keyboard path. Fixed by adding a default Action('ctrl-z') that calls os.kill(getpid(), SIGTSTP), routing the byte through the existing handler chain. End-to-end Ctrl-Z+fg now restores the screen identically.
        2) Async result delivery (apply_children_results, apply_preview_result) marked the visible-tree dirty but never set _needs_redraw, so the main loop never rendered after a worker wake -- only after the next user keystroke. Tests previously worked around this with explicit Ctrl-L kicks. Fixed by adding 'list'/'preview' to _needs_redraw on result delivery.
        3) Same root cause: _do_expand and _do_select changed visible state without flagging redraw. Fixed similarly. Loading-placeholder test now sees the ⧗ row before children arrive.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Recipe browse-fs {#15}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 08:14:49 UTC

    `recipes/browse-fs` — filesystem browser, target ~80 lines.

    - get_children: lazy `os.scandir`, sorts dirs first, computes
      `item.size`/`item.mode`/`item.mtime` as extra attrs, `item.tag` is
      human-readable size for files.
    - get_preview: head 4096 bytes for files, `os.listdir` for dirs.
    - Actions: `e:Edit` ($EDITOR), `o:Open` (xdg-open),
      `d:Delete` with `ctx.confirm`.
    - Background mtime watcher refreshes changed dirs (poll-based; inotify
      is a phase-3 polish opportunity).
    - Shebang `#!/usr/bin/env -S browse-tui --python`.
    - Manual smoke: `chmod +x recipes/browse-fs && ./recipes/browse-fs ~`.

    * ## Comments {#15:comments}

      * Implementation complete. {#15:comment:54}

        Files:
        - recipes/browse-fs (130 lines, executable)
        - test/ui/test_recipe_browse_fs.py (2 tests, ~80 lines)
        Test results:
        - All 290 tests pass (was 288 + 2 new). 3-run flakiness check: 3/3 stable.
        - New tests run in ~2.3s.
        Recipe shape:
        - get_children: lazy os.scandir; dirs first then files alphabetical;
          sets item.size/mode/mtime as extra attrs; tag = human_size for files,
          empty (cyan) for dirs; trailing '/' on dir titles.
        - get_preview: head 4096 bytes of file or os.listdir for dir.
        - Actions: e:Edit (cursor, $EDITOR), o:Open (targets, xdg-open),
          d:Delete (targets, ctx.confirm). on_enter='action:e'.
        - Watcher: 1s poll over browser._state._children.keys();
          refresh(d) when mtime differs from baseline.
        Notes / caveats / phase-3 follow-ups:
        - The shebang `#!/usr/bin/env -S browse-tui --python` requires the user
          to invoke as `./recipes/browse-fs -- <PATH>`. Without `--`, browse-tui's
          argparse rejects the unknown positional. A phase-3 polish opportunity:
          argparse.parse_known_args + appended extras when --python is used, so
          that `./recipes/browse-fs ~` works directly.
        - Watcher initial-tick race: the watcher records its mtime baseline on
          the first tick (~1s after start). Mutations between cache load and
          first tick are absorbed silently. The test sleeps 1.5s before the
          mutation to guarantee the change happens after the baseline is set.
          Phase-3 polish: hook the cache-population path so the watcher's
          baseline is the cache-load time, eliminating this race.
        - Phase-3 inotify: replace the 1s polling with inotify watches keyed on
          cache contents, with fallback to polling on platforms without it.
        - Symlink handling: symlinks are not resolved (follow_symlinks=False);
          broken symlinks render with whatever stat error surfaces. Fine for
          v1; may want a [link] tag in phase 3.
        - Permission errors mid-browse: surface via the `__err__:<path>` synthetic
          item — keeps the UI usable. Could be improved with a styled overlay
          in phase 3.
        - xdg-open is not testable in CI; the action exists but only the existence
          is verified, not the positive path.
        Smoke test:
        - Direct invocation `./browse-tui --python recipes/browse-fs -- <PATH>`
          launches and renders correctly under tmux (verified by the new tests).
        - Shebang form (`./recipes/browse-fs -- <PATH>` with browse-tui on PATH)
          reaches Browser.run(); fails only on tcgetattr when stdin is /dev/null
          (expected; no controlling terminal in non-TTY contexts).

  * ## Ticket: Task: Multi-select {#17}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 08:36:21 UTC

    `space` toggles selection (cursor moves down). `alt-space` toggles + up.
    `ctrl-a` selects all visible. `ctrl-n` deselects all. `*` marker on
    rendered rows. `[N]` selection count in info bar.
    `Action.requires=='targets'` uses selection or cursor fallback.
    UI tests cover all key paths.

    * ## Comments {#17:comments}

      * Implemented multi-select keybindings: space (toggle+down, requires=cursor), alt- (toggle+up, requires=cursor), ctrl-a (select all visible, requires=none), ctrl-n (clear, requires=none).   * ## Ticket: Task: ctx.pick (fzf-style sub-picker) {#20}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 09:14:29 UTC

    Filter prompt on info bar, list overlaid in preview pane, returns
    chosen string or `None`. Used by recipes for status pickers etc.
    Tests: filter matching, cursor up/down, enter, esc.

    * ## Comments {#20:comments}

      * Implemented Context.pick() and _pick_on_info_bar helper in src-tui/060-context.py. Helper takes a _read_key= injection seam for deterministic unit testing. {#20:comment:58}

        Decisions:
        - Resize handling inside the picker: minimal-viable. The loop continues on _notify/SIGWINCH and re-derives the layout each iteration, so a resize repaints on the next render. No explicit g_resize_flag check (phase-3 polish).
        - Layout overlap: when info_row == prev_top (no children-grid pane), the prompt and the options would overdraw the same row. The picker reserves the info_row for the prompt and shifts options down by one (options_top = prev_top + 1).
        - Unit-test terminal stub: a _StubTerminal context manager that swaps out move/clear_line/set_style/reset_style/write/flush/term_size to no-ops on the loaded module. The pure layout_panes function is left intact so geometry is computed real.
        - Tests added:
          * test/unit/test_pick.py: 18 tests (3 headless, 15 loop logic).
          * test/ui/test_pick.py: 3 tmux end-to-end tests via test/ui/recipes/pick_demo.py.
        Constraints respected: no typeahead-by-fragment, no preview content under the picker, no paging, no re-entrancy support (documented in pick docstring).
        346 baseline → 367 total (21 new). 3-run flakiness check stable. ./build-tui.sh && ./browse-tui --version succeeds.

  * ## Ticket: Task: ctx.insert (insert mode for placement) {#21}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 09:29:38 UTC

    Full insert mode with placement marker, depth manipulation via
    `right/left`, `home/end/pgup/pgdn` movement, sibling vs child resolution,
    callback receives `(relation, dest_id)`. Port `_resolve_insert` from
    plan-tui (per-position, per-depth coverage).

    * ## Comments {#21:comments}

      * Implementation complete. {#21:comment:59}

        Files modified:
        - src-tui/040-state.py: added Browser._insert_{mode,pos,depth,callback,label} fields; added pure helpers auto_insert_depth() and resolve_insert(); wired _handle_insert_key into Browser.run() main loop ahead of dispatch_key.
        - src-tui/050-render.py: added _INSERT_MARKER_ID sentinel; render_list injects a synthetic VisibleEntry(kind='insert_marker') at insert_pos when insert_mode is True, rendered yellow-on-blue bold per plan-tui.
        - src-tui/060-context.py: added Context.insert(label, on_confirm) entry point; headless is no-op, empty-visible-list is no-op, sets up state at gap (cursor + 1) with auto_insert_depth.
        - src-tui/070-actions.py: added _handle_insert_key (full key dispatcher mirroring plan-tui 070-main.py:98-249) plus _list_pane_height helper for pgup/pgdn page sizing.
        Tests added:
        - test/unit/test_insert_resolution.py: 31 unit tests for auto_insert_depth and resolve_insert covering empty/pos-zero/sibling/child/outdent/scope-root/deep-tree paths.
        - test/unit/test_insert_mode.py: 16 tests for Context.insert entry + _handle_insert_key (movement, indent/outdent, confirm/cancel).
        - test/ui/test_insert_mode.py + test/ui/recipes/insert_demo.py: 3 UI tests (marker visible, enter confirms with 'after:a', esc cancels).
        Test totals: 367 baseline -> 417 total (50 new). 3-run flakiness check stable.
        Key decisions:
        1. Outdent walks the visible list (not parent metadata) since browse-tui's VisibleEntry has no 'parent' field. Mirrors plan-tui's id_map walk by using DFS-ordering: most recent earlier row at depth d is the unique enclosing ancestor at that depth. Tested in test_outdent_with_multiple_subtrees_finds_correct_ancestor.
        2. Skipping scope_root rows: above-is-scope_root => ('before', vis[pos]) or (None,None); outdent walks past scope_root => (None,None) (mirrors plan-tui's 'don't reference Project' behavior).
        3. _handle_insert_key returns True for all keys (handled or not). Unhandled keys are swallowed silently — plan-tui forwards to the normal-mode handler; we deferred that polish per the ticket's phase-2 simplification note.
        4. _INSERT_MARKER_ID is object() (sentinel) instead of plan-tui's -1 — keeps sentinel distinguishable from any user-supplied id (mirrors _PENDING_PLACEHOLDER_ID pattern).
        5. UI test gotcha: tmux 'send-keys Escape' followed quickly by another send may coalesce into ESC+CHAR which the terminal layer reads as alt-CHAR. Worked around by sending raw \x1b for Esc and polling for the marker disappearing before sending the follow-up key. Same root cause as the test_search.py wait_for after Esc.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Pending.cancel() (non-strict) {#30}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 10:52:34 UTC

    Allow chains to be cancelled — worker still completes the in-flight
    fetch, but the chain doesn't fire. Useful for "user moved on, don't
    auto-cursor-to a stale result".

    * ## Comments {#30:comments}

      * Implemented Pending.cancel() with non-strict semantics: cancel() marks _cancelled=True, eagerly clears _chain (so queued pre-cancel callbacks are dropped before _resolve), and .then() after cancel becomes a no-op that still returns self for chain ergonomics. _resolve still flips _done=True even when cancelled (so worker.done remains observable) but skips firing callbacks. Added Browser.cancel(*pendings) sugar. Re-entrant edge case (a callback calls cancel() during _resolve iteration): already-snapshotted callbacks continue to run -- we don't abort mid-loop -- but any .then() registered by a later callback no-ops. Documented in the docstring. 9 new unit tests in test_pending.py + 4 new async tests in test_cancel.py. Total 527 tests, 3-run stable. {#30:comment:67}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Bonus recipes (optional) {#34}

        status: done
        created: 2026-04-30 03:43:27 UTC
        updated: 2026-04-30 11:39:34 UTC

    `browse-jira`, `browse-procs`, `browse-git` — if time permits.
    Each ~50–100 lines; demonstrates a different data source.

    * ## Comments {#34:comments}

      * Implemented all three bonus recipes: {#34:comment:71}

        - recipes/browse-procs (139 lines): builds a hierarchical process tree from `ps -eo pid,ppid,user,comm`, with PID 1 as the root (Linux) and a fallback to ppid=0 children excluding the kernel-thread PID 2. Preview reads /proc/<pid>/status. Custom action k:Kill sends SIGTERM with a y/n confirm. Uses bool() around has_children to coerce the truthy-list pattern.
        - recipes/browse-git (111 lines): three-level commit -> file -> diff hierarchy via id-shape dispatch (str without ':' = commit sha, str with ':' = file-in-commit). Top-level shows `git log --oneline -n 50`; expanding a commit lists files via `git show --name-only --format=`; preview at level 2 is the unified diff. Degrades gracefully with a single error Item if git is missing or cwd isn't a repo.
        - recipes/browse-jira (128 lines): sketch over the `jira list` CLI. Tolerant parser that accepts pipe-separated, tab-separated, or whitespace-multi-column rows; skips header/separator lines. Falls through to a friendly error Item when the CLI is missing, exits non-zero, or returns no rows. Custom o:Open action invokes $BROWSER (or xdg-open) with the ticket key.
        Tests: 4 new UI tests under test/ui/ — 2 for browse-procs (PID 1 renders, /proc status preview), 2 for browse-git (commits list, drill into files via Right). Both gate on tmux + tool presence with setUpModule guards. No tests for browse-jira (environment-dependent — depends on jira CLI auth/output).
        Docs: docs/recipes.md updated with three new recipe sections matching the existing style (one-line, demonstrates list, usage, keys, source link). Header bumped from 'three production-quality recipes' to 'six recipes — three production-quality plus three short bonus recipes'.
        Total tests: 537 (533 baseline + 4 new). 3-run flakiness check: all green. Decisions of note:
        - browse-procs: chose PID 1 (init) as the canonical root rather than expanding all ppid=0 entries; cleaner UX, hides kernel threads (which are mostly noise) but keeps them reachable as descendants of PID 2 if the user drills.
        - browse-git: id shape uses ':' as the separator since shas never contain it; the children-pane label visually duplicates the path-as-tag with the path-as-title but it's acceptable readability.
        - browse-jira: parser is intentionally lenient because jira CLIs differ — added a docstring note pointing recipes that need stricter parsing at a JSON template variant. Open action uses $BROWSER first, xdg-open as fallback.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Fix held-key blank-state bug {#77}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-01 01:15:36 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-01 02:14:28 UTC

    Holding up or down arrow rapidly can leave some rendered rows in a
    blank state — the renderer falls behind the key stream and a visible
    row fails to repaint. plan-tui had this same issue and fixed it.

    Investigate:
      - `../plan-source/src-tui/050-render.py` — does it batch redraws?
        Look for the dirty flag handling around `_scroll_offset`.
      - `../plan-source/.PLAN.md` and git log in `../plan-source` for
        commits with terms like 'blank', 'render', 'scroll', 'flicker'.
      - The likely cause is `render_partial` clearing rows it later writes
        nothing to — when the cursor scrolls past the buffered _scroll_offset,
        the next render_partial may not re-emit those rows.

    Acceptance: holding arrow keys for several seconds at high repeat
    rate produces no blank rows. Add a stress test (UI test that sends
    100+ arrow keys and inspects final screen).

    * ## Comments {#77:comments}

      * Investigation: ran 3-stress test variations (200 Down, mixed Down/Up/Pg, 300 Down with preview pane). All pass on current code. The bug doesn't reproduce because browse-tui's render_list iterates 'for row_idx in range(height): clear_line(); write(...)' — every row in the list pane is unconditionally re-cleared and re-written on every render_list call. Plan-tui's render_list does the same; the bug must have manifested in a different code path / earlier rev that has already been ported correctly. Adding the stress tests as a regression net so any future partial-row optimisation that re-introduces the bug fails fast. {#77:comment:86}

      * Resolution: Added test/ui/test_held_key_stress.py with 3 stress tests (200 batched Down presses, mixed Down/Up/PageDown/PageUp, 300 Down with preview pane active). All pass deterministically (5/5 isolated runs, 3/3 full suite runs). Total tests: 559 (was 556, +3). {#77:comment:87}

        Root-cause analysis: browse-tui's render_list (in 050-render.py) already does the right thing — it iterates 'for row_idx in range(height): clear_line(); write(content)' so every row is unconditionally cleared and rewritten on every render_list call. plan-tui's render_list does the same. The blank-row failure mode (render_partial clearing rows it later writes nothing to) cannot occur in this implementation. The drain-before-render ordering in Browser.run() (drain_main_queue + apply_children_results + apply_preview_result run before render_partial / render_full each loop iteration) was already correct.
        Preventive change: _do_cursor_to in 040-state.py now flags list/children/preview redraws on a successful cursor move. Without it, an external thread calling browser.cursor_to(id) would move the cursor but the screen wouldn't update until the next user keystroke — a related (though milder) form of stale-render bug that the same stress test would have surfaced if exercised through that API.
        Files modified:
          - test/ui/test_held_key_stress.py (new, 3 tests)
          - src-tui/040-state.py (_do_cursor_to flags redraws)

  * ## Ticket: Task: Recipe-pluggable help text and hotkey descriptions {#79}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-01 01:15:36 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-01 02:42:56 UTC

    [BRAINSTORM-FIRST. Do not dispatch this ticket until the design is
    agreed with the user.]

    Recipes need to extend the help text shown by `--help` and `?`.
    Currently `--help` prints argparse usage + the static `_HELP_TEXT`
    keybindings reference; `?` shows `_HELP_TEXT` in the preview pane.
    Recipe-specific actions (e.g., browse-plan's e:Edit, s:Status,
    c:Create) are invisible in the help.

    Required for both CLI and API modes. Each hotkey definition should
    be able to carry a description (Action.label exists; may need richer
    field). Recipes should also be able to add common prose
    (intro/outro/notes).

    Design dimensions:
      - what does a recipe contribute (auto-derived from Action vs
        explicit help_intro/help_outro vs full takeover)
      - hotkey description: stay with Action.label (one-liner) or add
        a richer Action.help field
      - CLI flags: --help-intro / --help-outro vs --help-text path/to/file
      - help output structure: where do recipe additions appear (top,
        middle ACTIONS section, bottom)
      - same content in --help and ? or different (--help could include
        CLI flag reference; ? skips it)

    Brainstorm with the user before implementing.

    * ## Comments {#79:comments}

      * Design agreed (brainstormed): {#79:comment:80}

        Approach A — auto-derive ACTIONS section + optional intro/outro prose.
        API:
          Browser(help_intro=str|None, help_outro=str|None)
          Action.label is the canonical short description (~60 chars max);
            documented in the dataclass docstring.
        CLI flags:
          --help-intro TEXT_OR_@PATH
          --help-outro TEXT_OR_@PATH
          '@PATH' loads the prose from a file (avoids command-line length limits).
          '@@PREFIX' escapes literal '@'-prefixed text (so '@@foo' -> '@foo' literal).
        Help composer (new helper, e.g. compose_help_text(browser, *, include_usage)):
          [help_intro]              (omitted if None)
          NAVIGATION                (built-in defaults — unchanged)
          PREVIEW
          SEARCH
          SELECTION
          OTHER
          CUSTOM ACTIONS            (only if browser.actions is non-empty)
            e   Edit in \$EDITOR    (action.label)
            d   Delete with confirm
          [help_outro]              (omitted if None)
        --help output: argparse usage + composed help text (include_usage=True).
        '?' in TUI:    composed help text only (include_usage=False), skipping
                       argparse usage which is irrelevant once the app is running.
        Sections without content are omitted (no empty 'CUSTOM ACTIONS' header).
      * Implemented Approach A. {#79:comment:89}

        Files modified:
        - src-tui/070-actions.py: added Action.section field; tagged each default action.
        - src-tui/040-state.py: added Browser(help_intro=, help_outro=) kwargs.
        - src-tui/050-render.py: added compose_help_text + _format_help_section; wired ? mode to use composer; reduced static _HELP_TEXT to a minimal fallback.
        - src-tui/080-cli.py: added --help-intro / --help-outro flags; _resolve_help_text helper (@PATH file load, @@ escape, missing-file SystemExit); _build_browser_for_help so --help reflects -a / --help-intro / --help-outro flags; threaded help_intro/help_outro through _build_lazy_browser and _build_eager_browser.
        - recipes/browse-fs, browse-plan, browse-claude, browse-procs, browse-git, browse-jira: added help_intro prose; tightened action labels.
        - test/unit/test_help_text.py (new): 19 tests covering Action.section, compose_help_text, _resolve_help_text.
        - test/ui/test_help_text.py (new): 8 tests covering --help and ? in TUI.
        - test/unit/test_cli.py: updated test_help_includes_keybindings (the deprecated "Default keybindings" header is gone; checks section headers instead).
        - test/ui/snapshots/help_mode.txt: regenerated (composer output replaces the static block).
        Test count: 559 -> 586 (+27). 3-run flakiness check stable. ./browse-tui --version + ./browse-tui --help -a "e:Edit:true" both work.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Preview should replace unprintable characters with ? {#82}

        updated: 2026-05-01 02:59:17 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-01 01:38:33 UTC

    Preview pane currently passes raw bytes through after .decode('utf-8',
    errors='replace'). Files containing control characters (e.g., binary
    files, log files with \\x01-\\x1f sequences, terminals captured raw)
    display garbled output that can break the renderer's column tracking
    and emit ANSI escape sequences from the file content into the
    terminal — a real injection vector if you preview untrusted files.

    Replace any character with code < 32 (i.e., chr(0)..chr(31)) with '?'
    EXCEPT tab (\\x09) and newline (\\x0a). Tab gets passed through (the
    renderer already converts to spaces) or replaced consistently. Newline
    must be preserved (it's the line separator).

    Apply in src-tui/050-render.py inside _preview_lines (or wherever the
    preview text is finalised before write()).

    Tests:
      - unit: preview text containing \\x00-\\x08, \\x0b-\\x1f gets ?
              replacement; tab and newline preserved.
      - unit: preview text with embedded ANSI escape (\\x1b[31m) gets
              escape replaced with ? so we don't render attacker-controlled
              colour into the terminal.
      - UI: preview a file with binary content — pane shows ? markers,
            no terminal weirdness.

    Acceptance: previewing /bin/ls or any binary doesn't garble the screen
    or change colours; control chars become ?.

    * ## Comments {#82:comments}

      * Implemented _sanitize_preview helper (str.maketrans-based) in 050-render.py and routed render_preview's text source (per-item preview, error text, help) through it before line-wrapping. Defangs all control chars < 32 except tab/LF, plus DEL (0x7f). Tests added: test/unit/test_preview_sanitize.py (13 unit cases) + test/ui/test_preview_safety.py (2 UI cases — binary preview shows ? markers; literal ANSI escape becomes harmless text). Total tests 601/601 (was 586). 3-run flakiness check stable. Manual smoke against /bin/ls confirms cursor row intact and no foreign ANSI escapes leak into the capture-with-colours output. {#82:comment:90}

* ## Ticket: Task: -h short flag should display recipe help text and custom actions {#91}

      updated: 2026-05-02 01:52:46 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-02 01:42:00 UTC

  The CLI's '-h' short flag (and likely '--help' for recipes) does not
  include recipe-defined keybindings or help_intro/help_outro:

    ./browse-tui -h                       (short form — verify works)
    ./browse-tui -a 'k:label:cmd' -h      (custom actions should appear)
    ./recipes/browse-fs -h                (recipe — currently ignored;
                                           recipe's main() runs without
                                           argparse and -h falls into
                                           sys.argv where Browser ignores
                                           it, dropping the user into TUI
                                           mode)

  Investigate:
    1. Does './browse-tui -h' work today (argparse short form)? If yes,
       no fix needed at the binary level.
    2. Does './browse-tui -a 'k:label:cmd' -h' include 'k' in CUSTOM
       ACTIONS? Ticket #79 wired this for --help; verify -h reaches the
       same path.
    3. Does './recipes/browse-fs -h' show the recipe's help_intro and
       custom-action labels? Likely NO — recipes don't argparse their
       own argv; Browser doesn't intercept -h either.

  Fix:
    - Binary: -h should work via argparse short form; restore if broken.
    - Recipes: Browser.run() (or constructor) should detect '-h' or
      '--help' in sys.argv on entry and print the composed help text +
      exit 0 without entering the TUI. This zero-change-for-recipes
      approach is preferred over a manual helper.

  Acceptance:
    - './recipes/browse-fs -h' prints intro + section headers (incl.
      NAVIGATION, OTHER, CUSTOM ACTIONS with e:Edit, o:Open, d:Delete)
      and exits 0.
    - './recipes/browse-fs --help' same.
    - './browse-tui -a 'foo:Foo:true' -h' prints CUSTOM ACTIONS with
      'Foo'.
    - In-app '?' overlay still works as before.

  Tests:
    - Unit: integration test constructing a Browser with actions and
      verifying the help-text auto-detect path on Browser.run().
    - UI / subprocess: run './recipes/browse-fs -h' and assert exit 0
      + intro string in stdout.

  * ## Comments {#91:comments}

    * Implemented Browser.run() auto-detect of -h/--help in sys.argv[1:] (src-tui/040-state.py). Recipes that don't argparse their own argv now get recipe-aware help (intro/outro + CUSTOM ACTIONS) for free without entering the TUI loop. Also updated main() in src-tui/080-cli.py: when --python is set, args.help is forwarded to the recipe (appended to extras as --help) instead of being short-circuited to print binary help — otherwise the recipe's contributions would never appear. Test loader in test/unit/test_help_text.py injects compose_help_text onto the _state module (Browser.run uses bare-name resolution like other render functions). Tests added: 8 unit tests in test/unit/test_help_text.py (TestRunDetectsHelpFlag) covering -h/--help short-circuit, mid-position detection, custom-action visibility, intro/outro rendering, and negative cases (--help-intro substring must not match). 5 subprocess UI tests in test/ui/test_help_text.py (TestRecipeHelpFlag) covering both forms via --, both forms at top level, and recipe-with-own-argparse compatibility. Total: 614 tests (was 601, +13). 3-run flakiness check stable. {#91:comment:92}

* ## Ticket: Task: show_ids knob + drop '#' / suppress id when id==title {#93}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 01:55:08 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-05 02:18:58 UTC

  Default item renderer always emits `'#{id} title'`. For file-style
  recipes (id == title), this produces noise like `#README.md README.md`.
  The `#` itself is plan-tui-specific (GitHub issue convention) and
  doesn't generalize to PIDs, SHAs, paths, etc.

  Fix: drop the `#` literal everywhere and suppress the id segment when
  `str(item.id) == item.title`. Add a `show_ids` knob with three modes:
  `always` / `auto` (default) / `never`, exposed both on `Browser` and
  via CLI flag `--show-ids`.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Update render layer {#94}

* ## Ticket: Task: Reset preview state on cursor move (fix #82-followup) {#101}

      updated: 2026-05-05 06:04:29 UTC
      status: done

* ## Ticket: Task: Pass args after --python <recipe> straight to the recipe (no -- needed) {#106}

      updated: 2026-05-05 06:13:18 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 06:08:59 UTC

  Today every arg before -- is parsed by the binary and only args after -- reach the recipe. That's gdb-style and surprises users; e.g. "browse-tui --python recipes/browse-fs ~/foo" treats ~/foo as a binary positional.

  New rule: when --python SCRIPT appears in argv, everything after the script path becomes the recipe's argv verbatim. Keep -- working as a backward-compatible no-op (strip one leading --).

  Files: src-tui/080-cli.py (parse_args). Update test_cli.py with the new contract; add a test that confirms the no-dashes form works.

* ## Ticket: Task: Mouse support: click-to-position cursor, wheel scrolls pane under mouse {#117}

      updated: 2026-05-05 08:11:04 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 07:53:09 UTC

  Behavior:
  - Click on list row → state.cursor = clicked row.
  - Click on preview → dismiss help mode if active, else no-op.
  - Click on children grid / info row / separator → no-op.
  - Wheel on list → ±3 _list_scroll. Cursor unchanged (decoupled).
  - Wheel on preview → ±3 _preview_scroll (same channel as shift-up/down).
  - Wheel on children grid → no-op.

  Modal states (insert / search / picker) ignore mouse events.

  After a wheel scroll, cursor may be off-screen. Next cursor-moving key snaps viewport to cursor automatically (centralized in main loop).

* ## Ticket: Task: Fix: preview pane stays blank when initial children fetch exceeds startup wait window {#124}

      updated: 2026-05-05 08:24:22 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 08:20:33 UTC

  Repro: a recipe whose get_children for the root takes >500ms returns; cursor lands on row 0 once children arrive but the preview pane stays empty until the user presses a key.

  Cause: _update_preview_for_cursor / _update_children_for_cursor only run after key dispatch in the main loop. When children arrive via worker _notify, drain/apply lands them but the cursor-derived fetches never fire — vis was empty at the pre-loop initial call, so cursor=0 mapped to no item.

  Fix: move both updaters to the top of the main loop (after apply_*). They're idempotent (skip when _preview_req already targets the cursor item), so the hot path is unchanged.

* ## Ticket: Task: Clamp state.cursor to visible-list length after apply_children_results {#125}

      updated: 2026-05-05 08:39:37 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 08:34:21 UTC

  When apply_children_results lands a smaller children list (e.g., via watcher refresh / ctx.refresh), state.cursor can sit past the new visible-list end. Renderer skips it (no crash), but the cursor effectively disappears.

  Fix: after applying the cache update, clamp state.cursor to max(0, len(visible)-1).

  Skipped sibling fix A (snap-to-cursor on apply): it would override user wheel-scroll position. The renderer's bounds clamp on _list_scroll plus this clamp on cursor are sufficient for cursor-visibility in all cases where the user hasn't intentionally wheel-scrolled away.

* ## Ticket: Task: Hot preview-fetch loop introduced by #124: gate on _preview_cursor_id not _preview_req {#126}

      updated: 2026-05-05 09:29:35 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 08:50:45 UTC

  Symptom: idle browse-tui burns ~11% CPU. test_ctrl_z_then_fg_round_trip flakes ~70% of runs ('R' instead of 'S' post-fg).

  Cause: the preview worker clears self._preview_req to None after each fetch. _update_preview_for_cursor's check 'new_id != self._preview_req' therefore always fires (None != 'alpha'), kicking another fetch every main-loop iteration. Pre-#124 this was masked because the function only ran after key dispatch — between dispatches the cycle stalled.

  Fix: gate on self._preview_cursor_id (which is only updated when the cursor moves to a different item, not by the worker). Also reset _preview_cursor_id in _do_refresh so an explicit refresh forces re-fetch.

* ## Ticket: Task: SIGCONT handler deferred until next bytecode checkpoint after os.kill {#127}

      updated: 2026-05-05 09:29:27 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-05 09:29:10 UTC

  Found while investigating the suspend test flake post-#126 fix.

  After #126 removed the hot preview-fetch loop that was masking this, the suspend test (Ctrl-Z then fg) failed reliably: the screen stayed on the bash prompt instead of re-rendering the TUI.

  Root cause: in _handle_sigtstp, the last statement is os.kill(getpid(), SIGTSTP) — which causes the process to suspend. When SIGCONT resumes, the kernel returns from kill, but Python's RETURN_VALUE bytecode doesn't always trigger a signal-handler check. The queued _handle_sigcont thus only runs at the NEXT bytecode checkpoint, which can be deferred until the main-loop's read_key wakes for some other reason. By then the test has already captured a stale screen.

  Fix: add a trailing function call after os.kill in _handle_sigtstp. Re-asserting signal.signal(SIGCONT, _handle_sigcont) is harmless and self-documenting. The CALL bytecode reliably forces a signal-handler check, so SIGCONT processes synchronously on the resume path.

* ## Ticket: Task: Implement 4 split layouts with runtime switching {#144}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-06 05:45:13 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-06 07:53:58 UTC

  Add 4 selectable layouts (vertical, horizontal, mixed, preview-children) with runtime switching via Alt-1..4 and `\` cycle, plus `--split-type` CLI flag.

  **Design decisions agreed with user:**
  - Layouts: 1=vertical (list | children | preview — children sub-column up to 25% wide of the right-of-list area, hidden when no children), 2=horizontal (list/children/preview stacked, current default), 3=mixed (list+children stacked | preview), 4=preview-children (list | children+preview stacked)
  - Children pane cap: 25% of its sub-area along the relevant axis (width in v, height in h/m/pc)
  - Separators are first-class views with their own renderers; info bar lives in the bottom separator (saves one row)
  - Rect = {left, top, right, bottom} exclusive on right/bottom
  - Per-layout geometry functions, dispatched by `layout_panes(split=...)`. No engine class.
  - Min-size enforcement: degrade gracefully (hide children, then collapse preview) rather than crashing
  - CLI: `--split-type=TYPE` (h|v|m|pc|a, default auto). Auto resolved at startup: width >= 230 → vertical, else horizontal. Not auto-recomputed on resize.
  - Hotkeys: Alt-1/2/3/4 direct selection, `\` cycles 1→2→3→4→1
  - list_ratio (existing) stays as float fraction of primary axis (height for h, width for v/m/pc)

  * ## Comments {#144:comments}

    * All implementation subtickets closed (#145-#155, #163, #166, #167). One cosmetic follow-up open as #172 (separator junction connectors) — known limitation deferred per #147 design note. Smoke test #155 passed all 22 scenarios. Build clean, 868 tests pass. {#144:comment:174}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Introduce Rect type and per-layout geometry functions {#145}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 05:45:13 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 06:01:15 UTC

    Replace the row-based dict in `050-render.py:layout_panes()` with rectangle-based output.

    - Define `Rect` (NamedTuple or dataclass): `{left, top, right, bottom}` (exclusive right/bottom).
    - Implement four pure functions:
      - `_layout_vertical(cols, rows, *, list_ratio, show_preview, show_children, children_cols_needed)` — `list | children | preview`. Children is a column to the LEFT of preview, width capped at 25% of the right-of-list area; hidden when not active. Falls back to `list | preview` when children are inactive.
      - `_layout_horizontal(cols, rows, *, list_ratio, show_preview, show_children, children_rows_needed)` — current behavior, stacked
      - `_layout_mixed(cols, rows, *, list_ratio, show_preview, show_children, children_rows_needed)` — list+children left, preview right
      - `_layout_preview_children(cols, rows, *, list_ratio, show_preview, show_children, children_rows_needed)` — list left, children+preview right
    - Each returns dict with keys: `list`, `children`, `preview`, `sep_main`, `sep_inner`, `info_bar` (Rect or None). In layout 1, `sep_main` separates list from the right area; `sep_inner` separates children from preview when children are visible.
    - `layout_panes(cols, rows, *, split, ...)` dispatches by split type. Both `children_rows_needed` and `children_cols_needed` are accepted; only the relevant one is used per layout.
    - Children pane capped at 25% of its sub-area along the relevant axis (height in h/m/pc, width in v); uses min(needed, cap, 1).
    - Min-size enforcement: if the layout cannot fit minimums, hide children first; if still cannot fit, drop preview.
    - Backwards-compat shim: keep old keys (`list_top`, `list_height`, etc.) emitted alongside new rects until all callers migrate, OR migrate all callers in this ticket. (Pick whichever is smaller diff — likely all-callers in same ticket.)

    * ## Comments {#145:comments}

      * Implemented Rect type and four per-layout helpers (_layout_horizontal, _layout_vertical, _layout_mixed, _layout_preview_children). layout_panes now dispatches by split (default 'h' for back-compat). Returns a dict of Rects with keys list/children/preview/sep_main/sep_inner/info_bar (None when not applicable), plus cols/rows. Migrated all callers in 040/050/060/070 to the new keys (.top/.height/.bottom etc.). Updated test_render.py and test_children_grid.py and test_actions.py to use the new shape. Children cap dropped from 30% to 25% per spec; sep_main/sep_inner are emitted but not yet rendered (separator rendering is #147). All 743 unit tests pass; build is clean. {#145:comment:156}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Wire up children sub-pane in vertical/mixed/preview-children layouts {#149}

        status: done

        updated: 2026-05-06 06:28:31 UTC

    The 25%-cap children pane has a different placement per layout:

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 07:11:18 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 07:20:22 UTC

    Two bugs reported by user after testing:

    **Bug 1:** Interactive resize keys (`-` / `=` / `_` / `+`, action `_resize_list` in 070-actions.py) don't work in vertical layout. The current resize logic computes step from `list_h` and `prev_h` (rows), but in vertical layout the resize should adjust list WIDTH (cols), not height. Need to make `_resize_list` axis-aware based on `browser.split`.

    **Bug 2:** Alt-1 vertical layout doesn't show children at all. The current `_layout_vertical` in 050-render.py places children as a COLUMN between list and preview. The user clarifies the intended design is:

    > "The layout should be identical to Alt-2 with difference that children view occupies a fixed percentage from Preview Window."

    Interpreted: Alt-1 should be `list | (children-above-preview)` — i.e., outer vertical split, then within the right area children stacks above preview taking a fixed percentage (~25%) of the right area's height. This is structurally equivalent to layout `pc` (preview-children).

    Action: rewrite `_layout_vertical` to mirror `_layout_preview_children` — children inside right area, above preview. Keep `_layout_preview_children` as-is (Alt-4 may be consolidated/renamed later by user).

    After fix, also re-run the existing children-sub-pane tests (#149 added `test_vertical_children_is_column_between_list_and_preview` which is now wrong by design) and update them to reflect the new vertical shape.

  * ## Ticket: Fix: Auto layout resolution doesn't work; add tmux integration tests {#167}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 07:11:37 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 09:35:55 UTC

    User reports `--split-type=auto` (the default) doesn't appear to apply correctly. Investigate `_resolve_split_type` and the wiring through `_build_lazy_browser` / `_build_eager_browser` in 080-cli.py:
    - Confirm that the terminal width passed to `_resolve_split_type` is actually the live width at startup, not a fallback (80).
    - Confirm that the resolved split is being passed to `Browser(split=...)` and not overwritten.
    - Confirm `os.get_terminal_size()` returns the right value when invoked from the lazy/eager builder (the early-exit path for non-tty stdin may use the 80-col fallback).

    Add tmux-based integration tests in `test/ui/` (or appropriate test dir) that:
    - Launch browse-tui in a 240-col tmux pane and verify vertical layout is in use (e.g. by inspecting the rendered output for the right-side preview column or for `\` cycling behavior).
    - Launch in a 80-col pane and verify horizontal layout is in use.
    - Test `--split-type=h`, `--split-type=v`, `--split-type=m`, `--split-type=pc` explicit overrides.

    Look at existing tmux test fixtures in `test/ui/` for patterns to follow.

    * ## Comments {#167:comments}

      * Diagnosis: {#167:comment:169}

        - Reproduced extensively in tmux at 240x40, 200x40, 80x24, 230x40, 229x40 — both with `--root-cmd cat` (stdin piped) and `--children-cmd` (stdin tty). In all of these `os.get_terminal_size()` returned the correct width and auto resolved correctly to v at >=230, h below.
        - The one path I found that *did* return the 80-col fallback was when stdout is also piped: `printf ... | browse-tui --root-cmd cat | cat`. With both stdin and stdout as pipes, `os.get_terminal_size()` (which falls back to stdout, then stderr) raises OSError and run_tui used the hard-coded 80 fallback.
        - For the common interactive case the original code already worked. The user's report likely reflects either (a) a terminal slightly narrower than 230 cols where auto correctly chose horizontal but they expected vertical (a UX surprise, not a bug), or (b) a wrapped invocation path where stdout was redirected.
        Fix:
        - Added `_terminal_cols_for_auto()` in 080-cli.py. It tries `/dev/tty` first (TIOCGWINSZ ioctl) — that source is independent of the standard streams and works even when stdin AND stdout are both pipes. Falls back to `os.get_terminal_size()`, then `default=80`. `run_tui()` now calls this helper instead of inlining the get_terminal_size+except-OSError block.
        - The auto threshold (>=230) and timing (resolved once at startup, before Browser construction) are unchanged.
        Tests:
        - Added `test/ui/test_split_layout.py` with 10 tmux-driven tests covering: auto -> v at 240, auto -> h at 80, threshold boundary at 229/230, explicit `h`/`v`/`m`/`pc` overrides, long-form alias `horizontal`, and the `\\` cycle from h to a vertical mode.
        - Added 2 unit tests in `test/unit/test_cli.py::TestTerminalColsForAuto` covering the helper's contract and forced-fallback path.
        Files changed:
        - src-tui/080-cli.py (added helper, replaced the get_terminal_size call site)
        - test/ui/test_split_layout.py (new, 10 tests)
        - test/unit/test_cli.py (new TestTerminalColsForAuto class, 2 tests)
        Test counts: 868 total, 866 pass + 2 pre-existing failures (#163 — test_help_screen_shows_custom_actions, test_help_intro_and_outro_in_help_screen — independently confirmed they fail in a clean tree without #167's changes), 4 skipped.
      * Reopened by user: at 242 cols, auto-resolution still selects horizontal instead of vertical. The /dev/tty fallback added in the previous fix is not picking up the live width. Need deeper investigation — possibly tcgetpgrp/foreground-process check, or the file descriptor we're reading isn't the actual TTY. {#167:comment:175}

      * Followup: term_size() in 020-terminal.py also crashed when stdout was piped (OSError on os.get_terminal_size with default fd). Hardened term_size() to try fds 1/2/0 then /dev/tty before falling back to 80x24. test_auto_split_under_pipeline_at_242_cols now passes. {#167:comment:178}

      * STILL FAILING per user. Previous fixes (broader fallback chain, hardened term_size) did not resolve. Need to capture user's diagnostic output and find the actual cause. {#167:comment:179}

      * Root cause for ongoing report: Python recipes (--run-py) bypass run_tui() and construct Browser directly via runpy.run_path. Browser.__init__'s split default was 'h', so recipes always got horizontal regardless of terminal width. Fix: changed default to 'auto' and extended _clamp_split to resolve 'auto' against term_size() at construction. Now both CLI auto path and recipe path resolve identically. {#167:comment:182}

  * ## Ticket: Redesign Alt-1 vertical layout: children as full-height column listed one-per-row {#176}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 08:30:43 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 08:45:34 UTC

    Per user clarification, Alt-1 should NOT be the same as Alt-4 (children-above-preview). The intended design is:

    - Outer split: `list | children | preview` (3 columns).
    - Children column is on the LEFT of preview, occupying the FULL HEIGHT of the body (not nested inside preview area).
    - Children items are listed ONE PER ROW (vertical stack of names), not as a grid.

    ASCII sketch:
    ```
    +------+--------+----------------+
    | list | chld1  |    preview     |
    |      | chld2  |                |
    |      | chld3  |                |
    |      | ...    |                |
    +------+--------+----------------+
    | info bar                       |
    +--------------------------------+
    ```

    Required changes:
    1. Rewrite `_layout_vertical` in 050-render.py: 3-column shape `list | children | preview` with children column = up to 25% of right-of-list area width (or sized to longest child name, capped). Children Rect spans full body height (above info_bar).
    2. Add a children rendering mode for "list one per row" (vs current grid). The renderer should detect when it's in vertical layout (or accept an explicit param) and switch render style. Look at `render_children_grid` / similar in 050-render.py.
    3. Update children-pane tests in test_render.py to reflect new shape.
    4. Smoke-verify in vertical layout that children render correctly as a left column.

    Note: This makes Alt-1 distinct from Alt-4 again. Alt-4 (preview-children) keeps its current shape (children above preview within right area).

    * ## Comments {#176:comments}

      * Rewrote _layout_vertical as a 3-column shape (list | sep | children | sep | preview) where children is a full-height column. Added _children_list_cols_needed for width hint. Added render_children_list (one-per-row) and wired it into render_full/render_partial via browser.split=='v' check. Updated v-layout tests in test_render.py to assert new column geometry; added test_vertical_distinct_from_preview_children and TestRenderChildrenList. All unit tests pass; only known #167 failure remains. Smoke verified with children_grid.py recipe + Alt-1. {#176:comment:177}

* ## Ticket: Redraw optimization: row cache + synchronized output {#184}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-06 15:32:52 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-06 16:47:04 UTC

  Reduce flicker on rapid cursor movement and shrink bytes-on-the-wire over
  ssh. Two-buffer per-pane row cache (last vs current emitted bytes), whole-line
  redraw on change, BSU/ESU synchronized-output brackets, no `\e[2J` on
  `render_full`. Padding rules per row on cache miss:

  | Pane cache state | Pad after content + `\e[m` |
  |---|---|
  | `prev_rect is None` (first paint, empty screen) | nothing |
  | `prev_rect != current_rect` (resize / layout change) | full pad to pane right edge, OR `\e[K` if pane is rightmost |
  | `prev_rect == current_rect`, content shorter than `prev_emitted_visible_len` | pad to `prev_emitted_visible_len`, OR `\e[K` if rightmost |
  | content same width or wider | nothing |

  Ctrl-L emits `\e[2J`, clears all pane caches, requests `'all'` redraw —
  next render replicates the empty-screen first-paint path.

  Capture mechanism: row-buffer shim in `020-terminal.py`. `begin_row(pane_cache,
  rel_row, abs_row, left, right, *, rightmost)` flips a module-level capture
  flag so `write()`/`set_style()`/`reset_style()`/`move()` accumulate into
  `_row_buf`. `end_row()` compares to `pane_cache.lines[rel_row]`; on miss,
  emits `\e[<abs_row>;<left>H` + `_row_buf` + `\e[m` + (pad-or-`\e[K`),
  updates cache. Existing renderers wrap each row body in `begin_row`/
  `end_row`; `clear_columns(...)` and `move(row, left)` calls inside the row
  body become redundant and are dropped.

  Cache lives on `Browser._pane_cache: dict[str, PaneCache]`. `PaneCache`
  holds `rect: Rect | None`, `prev_rect: Rect | None`, `lines: list[(bytes, visible_len) | None]`.
  Per-pane invalidation: at `render_*` entry, if `cache.rect != current_rect`,
  rotate `prev_rect = cache.rect`, set fresh `rect`, reset `lines = [None]*height`.

  Separators and info_bar use the same shim — separator with unchanged rect
  emits zero bytes, delivering the "skip separator redraw when layout
  unchanged" optimization for free.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Row-buffer shim primitives in 020-terminal.py {#185}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 15:32:52 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 15:38:14 UTC

    Add the capture infrastructure that lets renderers stay nearly unchanged
    while their per-row writes get diffed against the cache.

    **API to add (in `src-tui/020-terminal.py`):**

    ```python
    def begin_row(pane_cache, rel_row, abs_row, left, right, *, rightmost):
        """Start capturing writes into a row buffer. Subsequent
        write()/set_style()/reset_style()/move() calls accumulate into
        a module-level _row_buf instead of stdout. Pair with end_row().
        Cannot nest."""

    def end_row():
        """Compare captured _row_buf to pane_cache.lines[rel_row].
        Cache miss: emit \e[<abs_row>;<left>H + _row_buf + \e[m +
        (pad-or-\e[K) and update cache.
        Cache hit: emit nothing.
        Reset capture state."""

    def begin_sync():
        """write('\033[?2026h')"""

    def end_sync():
        """write('\033[?2026l')"""
    ```

    **Padding logic in end_row** (only on cache MISS):
    - If `pane_cache.prev_rect is None`: emit nothing after `\e[m` (first paint).
    - Elif `pane_cache.prev_rect != pane_cache.rect`: pad to pane right edge,
      OR `\e[K` if `rightmost`. Cache stores `visible_len = pane_width`.
    - Elif new visible_len < cached visible_len: pad to cached visible_len,
      OR `\e[K` if rightmost. Cache stores `visible_len = max(new, cached_was_emitted)`.
    - Else: emit nothing. Cache stores new visible_len.

    Visible length = the count of *visible cells* the row would occupy, not
    the byte length (SGR sequences don't count). The shim needs a small
    helper to compute visible length from captured bytes — strip `\033[...]m`
    sequences. There's already similar logic in `_truncate_visible`; reuse
    or factor out a `_visible_len(s)` helper.

    **Module state:**

    ```python
    _row_capture_active: bool = False
    _row_buf: list[str] = []  # appended to by write()
    _row_meta: dict | None = None  # holds pane_cache, rel_row, abs_row, left, right, rightmost
    ```

    **`write()` change:** if `_row_capture_active`, append to `_row_buf` instead
    of `sys.stdout.write`. Other helpers (`set_style`, `reset_style`, `move`,
    `clear_line`, `clear_columns`) call `write()` so they're routed automatically.

    **Tests** (`test/unit/test_terminal_row_shim.py`):
    - begin_row + write 'hello' + end_row, empty cache → emits nothing (None
      sentinel rule? — actually first paint emits content, no pad). Verify.
    - Same content twice → second end_row emits zero bytes.
    - Different content second time → second end_row emits `\e[<r>;<c>H` +
      content + `\e[m`.
    - prev_rect != rect, content shorter than pane width → pad to pane width
      with spaces (non-rightmost) or `\e[K` (rightmost).
    - Visible-len tracking handles SGR sequences correctly.

    * ## Comments {#185:comments}

      * Implemented row-buffer shim primitives in src-tui/020-terminal.py: _visible_len(), begin_row(), end_row(), begin_sync(), end_sync(); plus module state _row_capture_active/_row_buf/_row_meta and a capture-aware write(). Tests in test/unit/test_terminal_row_shim.py (19 cases) cover first paint, cache hit/miss, rect change padding (rightmost \e[K vs pane-width spaces), steady-state shorter-content padding, SGR-aware visible-length, capture-state reset, nesting guard, and indirect writes via set_style. Full suite: 900 OK (4 unrelated skips). {#185:comment:193}

  * ## Ticket: Task: PaneCache + Browser._pane_cache + render_full/render_partial wiring {#186}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 15:32:52 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 15:48:00 UTC

    Add the cache structure and wire the BSU/ESU brackets into the render
    entry points.

    **In `src-tui/040-state.py`:**

    ```python
    @dataclass
    class PaneCache:
        rect: Rect | None = None
        prev_rect: Rect | None = None
        lines: list = field(default_factory=list)  # [(bytes, visible_len) | None]

        def invalidate(self, new_rect):
            """Rotate prev_rect, set new rect, reset lines."""
            self.prev_rect = self.rect
            self.rect = new_rect
            self.lines = [None] * new_rect.height

        def ensure(self, new_rect):
            """Idempotent invalidate-if-changed."""
            if self.rect != new_rect:
                self.invalidate(new_rect)
    ```

    `Browser.__init__`: add `self._pane_cache: dict[str, PaneCache] = {}`.

    **In `src-tui/050-render.py`:**

    `render_full`:
    - Drop `write('\033[2J')`.
    - First line: `begin_sync()`.
    - Last line before `flush()`: `end_sync()`.

    `render_partial`:
    - First line: `begin_sync()`.
    - Last line before `flush()`: `end_sync()`.

    Both pass per-pane `is_rightmost` flag into renderers. Compute it from
    layout: a pane is rightmost on its rows iff `pane_rect.right == layout['cols'] + 1`
    (Rect right is exclusive). Simpler: pass the layout dict to renderers and
    let them compute, OR add `is_rightmost: bool` to the Rect that the
    layout helpers fill in.

    Recommend: compute in `_layout_for` and store as `is_rightmost` in a sibling
    field per pane (e.g. layout dict gets `'list_rightmost': bool` etc.) so
    each renderer call site has the bool ready.

    **Test:** `render_full` on a fresh Browser does NOT emit `\033[2J`. Both
    `render_full` and `render_partial` start with `\e[?2026h` and end with
    `\e[?2026l`.

    * ## Comments {#186:comments}

      * Implemented PaneCache dataclass in 040-state.py, Browser._pane_cache dict init, _layout_for now computes per-pane *_rightmost flags, render_full and render_partial brackets bodies with begin_sync()/end_sync() and render_full no longer emits \e[2J. All renderer signatures (render_list, render_children_grid, render_children_list, render_preview, render_separator, render_info_bar) gained a kw-only rightmost: bool=False parameter, plumbed from _layout_for. Added test_state.py PaneCache + Browser._pane_cache init tests, and test_render.py BSU/ESU bracket tests. All 909 tests pass; build clean. {#186:comment:194}

    Both are single-pane edge cases.

    **`render_info_bar`:** treat as a one-row pane. PaneCache key `'info_bar'`,
    `rect.height = 1`. Wrap the single row in `begin_row`/`end_row`.

    **`render_separator`** in `050-render.py:1525`: vertical separator emits
    `│` per row across its rect height; horizontal emits `─` per col across
    rect width. Treat each as a pane:
    - Vertical sep_main / sep_inner: pane height = rect.height, each row is
      a single-cell `│`. Loop: `begin_row(...) / write('│') / end_row()`.
    - Horizontal sep (only when info bar is folded into top of children/preview
      in 'h' layout — currently this path doesn't exist in render_separator,
      info bar handles it). Verify and handle accordingly.

    Free byproduct: with unchanged rect, the cache lines all match → zero
    bytes emitted. This is the "skip separator redraw when layout unchanged"
    optimization that falls out automatically.

    Test: switch from one layout to another and back — second switch back
    leaves cache populated, separator emits zero bytes on next paint of the
    same layout.

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 15:32:52 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 16:43:40 UTC

    Comprehensive coverage of the cache + padding semantics.

    Cases:
    - **No-op repaint:** call `render_partial` twice in a row with no state
      change between → second call emits exactly `\e[?2026h` + `\e[?2026l`
      (and nothing else).
    - **Cursor move down 1 in list pane:** before/after stdout diff → exactly
      two row updates emitted (old cursor row + new cursor row), no other
      panes touched.
    - **First paint:** `render_full` on a fresh Browser → no `\e[K`, no
      trailing-space padding runs anywhere; visible bytes only.
    - **Resize:** mock `term_size` change → next `render_full` pads every
      row in panes whose rect changed (either trailing spaces to width or
      `\e[K` for rightmost).
    - **Layout switch (Alt-1 → Alt-3):** same rule as resize — changed-rect
      panes get full pad.
    - **`\e[m` always precedes pad/`\e[K`:** scan emitted bytes — every
      space-pad-run or `\e[K` is preceded by `\e[m`.
    - **Rightmost vs non-rightmost:** in 'v' layout, list pane is leftmost
      (uses spaces), preview is rightmost (uses `\e[K`).
    - **Ctrl-L:** `_redraw(ctx)` then `render_full` → `\e[2J` present, then
      content-only (no pads, no `\e[K`).
    - **Trailing-content-shrink:** row content becomes shorter than previous
      paint → padding to previous visible length (steady-state rule).

    Use existing test infrastructure (`_headless` Browser, capture stdout via
    `io.StringIO` or fixture).

* ## Ticket: Task: Children pane and inner separator stale cache when reappearing after disappearing {#200}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-06 20:55:14 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-06 21:03:05 UTC

  When the cursor moves from an item with children to an item without children
  (in 'v', 'm', 'pc' layouts), `_layout_*` returns `children_rect=None` and
  `sep_inner_rect=None`. The cells those panes occupied get reclaimed by the
  expanded `preview_rect` (which is wider in this state). The renderers for
  the absent panes are skipped, so their PaneCache is left untouched —
  `cache.rect` still holds the old rect from when they last painted.

  When the cursor moves BACK to a with-children item, `children_rect` /
  `sep_inner_rect` come back with the same shape as before. PaneCache.ensure()
  sees `cache.rect == new_rect` → no-op. `cache.prev_rect` was rotated forward
  on the prior paint, so it equals `cache.rect` → end_row takes the steady-state
  path. If the new content matches what's in the cache (e.g. same children
  list), end_row cache-hits and emits nothing.

  But the screen no longer has the old children content — the preview pane
  overwrote those cells while the children pane was hidden. The cache
  desyncs from the screen.

  Symptom: stale preview content remains in the children-pane and inner-sep
  cells; the children list and the `│` separator never get repainted.

  Bug applies to BOTH 'children' and 'sep_inner' caches.

  **Fix** (orchestrator-level): in render_full / render_partial, when
  layout['children'] is None or layout['sep_inner'] is None, drop the
  corresponding entry from browser._pane_cache. Next time the pane reappears,
  the cache is recreated fresh — ensure() invalidates with the new rect,
  prev_rect=None, end_row enters "rect changed, full pad" path (because the
  cache was just recreated; the very-first ensure rotates self.rect=None →
  prev_rect=None, then on subsequent same-rect paint prev_rect rolls forward).

  Wait — that gives "first paint, no pad". For the case where the screen has
  stale content (overwritten by preview), we WANT pad-to-pane-width to overwrite
  it. But "first paint" path emits no pad on the assumption of empty screen.

  Better fix: when dropping the cache entry, mark the area as "dirty stale
  content present." Or simpler: don't just drop the cache — invalidate it
  with the next-time rect equal to current rect. But we don't know the next
  rect.

  Cleanest fix: on render_full/render_partial entry, before invoking
  renderers, scan layout for panes whose rect transitioned non-None → None.
  For each such pane name, the area its cache covered is now owned by
  another pane. Mark by setting `pane_cache.rect = None, prev_rect = some_sentinel`
  so when the pane reappears, ensure() invalidates AND end_row sees
  prev_rect != rect (sentinel), takes "full pad" path, overwriting stale
  cells.

  Even simpler: when a pane disappears (becomes None in current layout but
  we have a non-None rect cached), set `pane_cache.rect = None` AND
  `pane_cache.prev_rect = <the_old_rect_or_a_dummy_non_None_value>`.
  Next time pane reappears: ensure(new_rect) sees self.rect=None, invalidate
  → prev_rect = self.rect = None. Hmm, that loses the dirty signal.

  Alternative: keep pane_cache.rect as the old rect, drop pane_cache.lines
  to all-None. Next time same rect: ensure no-op (rect matches), prev_rect
  was rolled forward → prev_rect == rect → steady-state. cached lines are
  None → end_row miss path, but takes the "else: no pad" branch (cached_visible
  is 0 since lines[rel_row] is None → 0). Hmm, that still gives no padding.

  The clean fix: when a pane disappears, set the cache entry to a state
  that on next reappear forces "rect changed, full pad" semantics. Specifically:
  set pane_cache.prev_rect to something != future_rect. Setting prev_rect = None
  doesn't work because that's "first paint, no pad". We need a non-None
  prev_rect that doesn't equal the future rect.

  Solution: use a SENTINEL Rect (e.g. Rect(-1,-1,-1,-1)) as prev_rect on
  disappear. This guarantees end_row sees prev_rect != rect → full pad path.
  Then on reappear:
    - ensure(new_rect): self.rect = old_rect ≠ new_rect (assuming layout changed)
      → invalidate → prev_rect = old_rect, rect = new_rect, lines = [None]*.
      Actually wait — we'd set self.rect to the old rect when the pane
      disappeared, so on reappear if the rect happens to be the same as
      pre-disappear, ensure() is a no-op. Then end_row sees prev_rect
      (sentinel) != rect → full pad. ✓
    - If rect differs (e.g. resize while pane was hidden), invalidate sets
      prev_rect = self.rect (the old rect), then end_row sees prev_rect ≠ rect
      → full pad. Also ✓.

  Implementation:
    When orchestrator finds layout[name] is None but cache has an entry:
      cache.prev_rect = _SENTINEL_RECT  # something that will never equal a real rect
      cache.lines = [None] * len(cache.lines)  # or 0; doesn't matter
    Next reappear: end_row's "full pad" branch fires for every row.

  **Tests to add (UI / tmux):**
  - Hover over an item WITH children → see children list rendered.
  - Move down to an item WITHOUT children → children pane disappears,
    preview expands into the area.
  - Move back UP to a with-children item → children pane reappears, content
    is correct, sep_inner is correct, no stale preview text leaking through.
  - Repeat several times — bounces between with/without children should be
    stable.

  Sub-tasks:

  * ## Ticket: Task: Add tmux UI test reproducing the bug {#201}

        updated: 2026-05-06 20:58:03 UTC

  * ## Ticket: Fix orchestrator: invalidate caches for disappeared panes {#202}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 20:55:14 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-06 21:01:43 UTC

    In src-tui/050-render.py render_full and render_partial, after the
    layout dict is computed and BEFORE renderers run:

    ```python
    _SENTINEL_RECT = Rect(-1, -1, -1, -1)  # module-level constant

    for name in ('children', 'sep_inner'):  # panes that can disappear
        if layout.get(name) is None:
            cache = browser._pane_cache.get(name)
            if cache is not None and cache.rect is not None:
                # Pane disappeared — its cells were overwritten by another
                # pane (e.g. preview). Force next reappear to full-pad.
                cache.prev_rect = _SENTINEL_RECT
                cache.lines = [None] * len(cache.lines)
    ```

    Or factor a helper `_mark_pane_disappeared(browser, name)` for clarity.

    Verify the new tmux test now PASSES. Run full test suite — no regressions
    expected.

    * ## Comments {#202:comments}

      * Fixed by adding _SENTINEL_RECT and _mark_disappeared_panes helper in 050-render.py. {#202:comment:205}

        When layout drops 'children' or 'sep_inner' (cursor moves onto a no-children item in v/m/pc layouts), the helper stamps the cache.rect with _SENTINEL_RECT(-1,-1,-1,-1). Next time the pane reappears with same geometry, ensure() sees rect mismatch -> invalidate() -> end_row takes the rect-changed full-pad path, clearing cells the preview pane overwrote.
        Used the rect-stamping approach (option 1 from ticket) rather than prev_rect, because ensure()'s elif branch would otherwise overwrite a sentinel placed in prev_rect on the very next paint where rect matched.
        Also guarded against double-stamping: if cache.rect is already _SENTINEL_RECT we skip (avoids zeroing lines on every paint while a pane stays absent).
        Tests:
        - test/ui/test_children_pane_redraw.py: both new tests now pass
        - ./run-tests.sh: 931 tests, OK (4 skipped) — no regressions
        - ./build-tui.sh: clean

* ## Ticket: Task: Splitters not redrawn when switching between layouts {#216}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-06 22:17:51 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-06 22:22:02 UTC

  Bug: Alt-1/2/3/4 layout switching leaves outer splitter (`sep_main`)
  missing in some cases.

  Root cause: `_mark_disappeared_panes` (050-render.py:277) handles only
  `('children', 'sep_inner')`. But `sep_main` is also `None` in layout 'h'
  and a `Rect` in 'v'/'m'/'pc' — so v→h leaves sep_main's cache with a
  stale rect, then h→v finds rect-match → ensure() no-op → end_row
  steady-state → content `│` matches cached `│` → cache HIT → emit nothing.
  Screen has list-pane spaces in those cells (from list's full-pad on
  shrink), so the splitter column appears blank.

  Same pattern would apply to `preview` if show_preview toggle puts it
  None and a later toggle brings it back at the same rect.

  Fix: generalize the disappear-handling to ALL pane caches, not just
  the hardcoded children/sep_inner. Iterate `browser._pane_cache` keys;
  for each whose `layout.get(name) is None`, stamp `cache.rect = _SENTINEL_RECT`.
