* ## Ticket: Task: Repainting/screen caching review findings {#220}

      updated: 2026-05-07 01:38:35 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-06 22:46:01 UTC

  Findings from a review of the per-pane row cache + synchronized output
  renderer (#184/#188 work + the #200 / #216 stale-cache follow-ups).

  The architecture is clean and the recent work has been thoroughly tested.
  These tickets capture issues that surfaced in the review.

  ## Foundational refactor (do first)

    - #228 PaneCache.update_rect() unifies cache lifecycle.
            Subsumes the orchestrator-level _mark_disappeared_panes and
            the per-renderer cache.ensure() into one method on PaneCache,
            called from a single _reconcile_pane_caches site after
            _layout_for. Closes #221 and #224 as part of its acceptance
            criteria.

  ## Independent issues (any order, after #228 if convenient)

    - #222 (medium) _visible_len counts code points, not display columns
            — wide-character padding bug in 020-terminal.
    - #223 (medium) cursor-move redraw triplet is bug-prone
            — regressed in #183; helper or collapse-to-'all'.
    - #225 (low, cleanup) redundant move/clear_line inside row capture
            — render_info_bar; same renderer as #228 touches.
    - #226 (low, latent) render_separator horizontal-cached only paints
            row 0 — same renderer as #228 touches.
    - #227 (note) _handle_sigcont signal-safety docstring cross-reference.

  ## Closed (subsumed by #228)

    - #224 (was: remove redundant cache.prev_rect commits)

  * ## Ticket: Task: Refactor: PaneCache.update_rect() — unify cache lifecycle (replaces _mark_disappeared_panes + per-renderer ensure) {#228}

        updated: 2026-05-07 00:26:26 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 23:53:42 UTC

    ## Motivation

    The current per-pane row cache has two separate sources of state mutation:

      1. **Per-renderer**: each pane renderer calls `cache.ensure(rect)` at
         its top — handles "rect changed since last paint" via Rect equality.
      2. **Orchestrator**: `_mark_disappeared_panes` (050-render.py:261) runs
         after `_layout_for` and stamps `_SENTINEL_RECT` on caches whose
         `layout.get(name) is None`.

    The split is what caused #221 (and #200 before it). The orchestrator's
    predicate `layout.get(name) is None` is the wrong question for caches
    whose USE is conditional on layout shape rather than just presence —
    most notably `'info_bar'`, where the layout key is non-None in 'h' (as
    the folded preview/children header) AND in 'v'/'m'/'pc' (as the
    standalone bottom row), but the standalone cache is only USED in the
    latter case. Cells overwritten by a neighbour during the unused frame
    remain visible after the cache returns to use, because the steady-state
    cache-hit path emits nothing.

    Position changes and size changes ARE handled today, but only because
    `cache.ensure(rect)` runs inside each renderer and `Rect.__eq__`
    compares all four fields. Same machinery; just at a different layer.

    ## Design

    Centralize cache state transitions on the `PaneCache` class. Replace
    both `cache.ensure(rect)` AND the orchestrator-level stamping with a
    single method:

    ```python
    class PaneCache:
        def update_rect(self, rect: Optional[Rect]) -> None:
            """Reconcile cache state with the pane's geometry for this frame.

              rect is None     → pane hidden this frame; stamp for
                                  reappear-full-pad on next use.
              rect == self.rect → no-op (steady state; roll prev_rect forward).
              rect != self.rect → rect changed (resize, move, or unhide);
                                  invalidate to new rect.
            """
            if rect is None:
                if self.rect is not None and self.rect != _SENTINEL_RECT:
                    self.rect = _SENTINEL_RECT
                    self.lines = []
                return
            if self.rect != rect:
                self.invalidate(rect)
            elif self.prev_rect != self.rect:
                self.prev_rect = self.rect
    ```

    `_SENTINEL_RECT` becomes a private detail of `PaneCache` (callers think
    in terms of `Rect | None`).

    ## Single dispatch site

    Replace `_mark_disappeared_panes(browser, layout)` with
    `_reconcile_pane_caches(browser, layout)`. This function owns the
    layout→cache mapping in ONE place — including the conditional cases:

    ```python
    def _reconcile_pane_caches(browser, layout):
        cache_rects = {
            'list':      layout.get('list'),
            'preview':   layout.get('preview'),
            'children':  layout.get('children'),
            'sep_main':  layout.get('sep_main'),
            'sep_inner': layout.get('sep_inner'),
        }
        # info_bar: same layout key, two different cache uses.
        if _info_bar_is_separate(layout) or not browser.show_preview:
            cache_rects['info_bar'] = layout.get('info_bar')
        else:
            cache_rects['info_bar'] = None  # folded into pane header

        for name, rect in cache_rects.items():
            cache = browser._pane_cache.setdefault(name, PaneCache())
            cache.update_rect(rect)
    ```

    Called once from `render_full` and `render_partial`, immediately after
    `_layout_for`, replacing the existing `_mark_disappeared_panes` call.

    ## Renderer migration

    Every renderer's first lines change from:

    ```python
    cache = browser._pane_cache.setdefault('list', PaneCache())
    cache.ensure(rect)
    ```

    to:

    ```python
    cache = browser._pane_cache['list']  # reconciled by orchestrator
    ```

    The end-of-renderer `cache.prev_rect = cache.rect` commits also go
    away (the elif branch in `update_rect` is the single point that
    rotates `prev_rect`). This closes #224 as part of the refactor.

    **Affected renderers** (050-render.py): `render_list`, `render_preview`,
    `render_children_grid`, `render_children_list`, `render_separator`,
    `render_info_bar`. The `cache.setdefault` + `cache.ensure` sites at
    lines 1103, 1275, 1417, 1559, 1706, 1817 collapse to lookups.

    ## Critical invariant

    `update_rect` must be called EXACTLY ONCE per cache per frame.
    Calling it twice (e.g., once from the orchestrator and once from the
    renderer) breaks the prev_rect rotation: the elif fires on the second
    call, putting a fresh-rect cache into steady-state regime in the
    same frame as the rect change, which under-pads.

    Migration discipline: search/replace every `cache.ensure(` in the
    render module to make sure no legacy call survives.

    ## Tickets this closes

      - #221 (info_bar v→h→v stale): the new conditional in
        `_reconcile_pane_caches` handles the case the old predicate missed.
      - #224 (redundant cache.prev_rect commits): subsumed by the
        single-rotation-point invariant.

    ## Acceptance criteria

      1. New unit tests in test_render_cache.py:
         - update_rect(None) on a populated cache stamps SENTINEL.
         - update_rect(same_rect) no-ops on first call after invalidate
           (matching pre-existing cache.ensure behaviour).
         - update_rect(same_rect) rolls prev_rect forward on the second
           call (steady-state engagement).
         - update_rect(new_rect) invalidates with prev_rect = old rect.
      2. New tmux UI test: v → h → v sequence asserts the preview-label
         string ("Preview") is present in the bottom row of the final
         capture (regression test seed for #221).
      3. All existing tests in test_render_cache.py and
         test_terminal_row_shim.py pass without modification.
      4. test_split_layout, test_render, and the ui/* test_*_redraw suites
         continue to pass — the change should be behaviourally invisible
         to any test that wasn't testing the (now-removed) two-layer split.

    ## Out of scope

      - SIGCONT/term_resume `_pane_cache.clear()` paths stay as-is
        (different concern: total reset because the actual screen content
        was destroyed, not because the layout changed).
      - Ctrl-L `_redraw` action stays as-is.
      - The padding regimes in `end_row` (020-terminal.py) don't move;
        `update_rect` just makes sure the right regime is selected.

    ## Suggested execution order

      1. Add `PaneCache.update_rect` + unit tests (040-state.py +
         test_state.py).
      2. Add `_reconcile_pane_caches` alongside the existing
         `_mark_disappeared_panes`, gated by a flag, so the migration can
         be staged. (Or skip the flag and do an atomic switch — the
         refactor is small.)
      3. Migrate each renderer to drop its `cache.ensure` and end-of-fn
         commit. Run tests after each migration.
      4. Delete `_mark_disappeared_panes` and the `_SENTINEL_RECT`
         module-level export from 050-render.py (move to 040-state.py as
         a private constant).
      5. Add the regression test for #221.
      6. Close #221 and #224.

    * ## Comments {#228:comments}

      * Implementation complete. Refactor: {#228:comment:233}

        - Added PaneCache.update_rect() in 040-state.py with three-branch reconciliation (hidden/steady/changed). _SENTINEL_RECT moved to 040-state.py as a private _SentinelRect duck-type instance (avoids forward dep on Rect).
        - Added _reconcile_pane_caches() in 050-render.py as the single dispatch site, called from render_full and render_partial. Reconciles 'list', 'preview', 'children', 'sep_main', 'sep_inner', 'info_bar' caches via update_rect.
        - Removed _mark_disappeared_panes(), the module-level _SENTINEL_RECT, and per-renderer cache.ensure()/cache.prev_rect=cache.rect commits from all six renderers (render_list, render_preview, render_children_grid, render_children_list, render_separator, render_info_bar).
        - Renderers now do 'cache = browser._pane_cache[name]' lookup only.
        Note on info_bar conditional: the ticket suggested a conditional in _reconcile_pane_caches that skips info_bar reconcile in 'h' layout (folded case). I removed that conditional — it broke render_partial's 'info' branch which uses the info_bar cache via render_info_bar(manage_cache=True) regardless of layout. The unconditional update_rect path correctly handles bug #221 because layout['info_bar'] rect DIFFERS between v (bottom row) and h (folded into pane header), so update_rect invalidates across switches. The bug #221 manifested under the OLD code because cache.ensure(same_rect) was a no-op when intermediate layouts didn't paint through that cache; the centralized update_rect catches the rect transition unconditionally.
        Tests added:
        - test/unit/test_state.py: TestPaneCacheUpdateRect (6 tests covering the three branches plus edge cases).
        - test/ui/test_children_pane_redraw.py: test_info_bar_redraws_after_v_h_v_round_trip (regression seed for #221).
        Tests modified: test/unit/test_render.py (TestSeparatorCacheZeroBytes added _reconcile helper for direct-renderer calls, _MockBrowser._pane_cache became a self-populating dict subclass for KeyError-free direct renderer tests).
        All 940 tests pass.

  * ## Ticket: Task: info_bar standalone cache stale after v→h→v: bottom row goes blank {#221}

        updated: 2026-05-06 23:55:59 UTC
        status: wontfix
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC

    **Severity**: high — confirmed bug, affects user-visible state.

    **Reproduction**: in any layout that has a standalone bottom info bar
    ('v'/'m'/'pc' with show_preview=True, OR 'h' with show_preview=False),
    switch to a layout that folds the info bar into a pane header ('h' with
    show_preview=True), then switch back. The bottom-row info bar (with the
    `Preview`/`Help` label, `[N]` selection count, scope crumb, search/hint
    text) does NOT repaint. The cells stay blank or show whatever the
    intervening layout's pane wrote there.

    Confirmed via probe (sequence: v render → h render → v render): final
    V output emits ZERO cursor-moves to the info_bar row, and a `"Preview"`
    substring search returns False even though the cache.lines[0] entry
    still contains the bytes that *would* be emitted.

    **Root cause**: `_mark_disappeared_panes` (050-render.py:282) stamps a
    cache as disappeared via `if layout.get(name) is None`. For
    `'info_bar'`, the layout entry is non-None in BOTH:
      - 'h' with show_preview=True: info_bar.top coincides with the
        preview/children pane's header row (folded; standalone cache is
        **not used** because render_full passes manage_cache=False via
        render_preview/render_children_*).
      - 'v'/'m'/'pc': info_bar is its own bottom row (standalone cache IS
        used; render_full calls render_info_bar with manage_cache=True).

    Same dict key, different semantics. The stamping check can't see the
    difference.

    Going v → h → v:
      1. V0: `_pane_cache['info_bar']` created with rect = bottom-row Rect.
         Painted, prev_rect rolled forward.
      2. H: standalone cache untouched. Preview pane (rightmost in 'h')
         extends to the bottom row and clears it via `\e[K` on first paint.
      3. V1: `_mark_disappeared_panes` doesn't stamp `'info_bar'` (layout
         entry non-None). cache.ensure(same rect) is a no-op. cache.lines[0]
         still has V0's bytes; new buf == cached → cache hit → emit nothing.
         Bottom row stays blank.

    **Existing test that DOESN'T catch this**: ui/test_children_pane_redraw.py::
    test_sep_main_redraws_after_layout_round_trip exercises the exact v→h→v
    sequence but only checks columns containing `│` separator runs.

    **Fix options** (any one resolves):
      1. Special-case `'info_bar'` in `_mark_disappeared_panes`: stamp it
         whenever `not _info_bar_is_separate(layout)` (i.e. when the
         standalone cache is not the one being used by the current layout).
      2. Track which caches were touched by the current render via
         `cache.setdefault` calls — at the end of render_full/render_partial,
         stamp every cache key NOT in the per-frame "used" set.
      3. Drop `_pane_cache` entirely on `set_split` (cheap; full repaint is
         already triggered via 'all').

    **Regression test**: tmux UI test that does v→h→v at default sizes,
    asserts the recipe's preview label string (e.g. "Preview") is present
    in the bottom row of the final capture. Bonus coverage: same shape for
    show_preview toggle (off → on → off) and for any path that flips
    `_info_bar_is_separate(layout)` between frames.

    * ## Comments {#221:comments}

      * Subsumed by #228 — the redesign centralizes cache lifecycle on PaneCache.update_rect() and includes this case in its acceptance criteria. Closing as wontfix; reopen if #228 ships without resolving it. {#221:comment:229}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cursor-move redraw triplet (list+children+preview) is bug-prone — collapse to helper or to all {#223}

        updated: 2026-05-07 01:17:25 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC

    **Severity**: medium — class-of-bug; one instance already regressed
    (#206 / commit 0c8769d).

    **Issue**: 070-actions.py contains the manually-written triplet

        ctx._browser._needs_redraw.add('list')
        ctx._browser._needs_redraw.add('children')
        ctx._browser._needs_redraw.add('preview')

    at ~20+ sites, anywhere a cursor move (or equivalent) fires. The
    pattern is hand-rolled; missing one entry (e.g. forgetting
    `'children'`) leaves the children pane stale until the next user
    keystroke. That exact bug shipped in `_nav_left`'s parent-jump branch
    and was fixed in commit 0c8769d (#183/#206/#207/#208).

    As long as the pattern stays hand-written, the next addition has the
    same trap.

    **Fix options**:
      1. Helper: `mark_cursor_changed(browser)` that sets all three flags.
         Replace every triplet site with the helper call. Future
         additions of cursor-move-side-effects don't need to remember the
         exact set.
      2. Collapse to `'all'`: just add `'all'` everywhere a cursor moves.
         The differential renderer makes redundant repaints near-free
         (no-op rows emit zero bytes between BSU/ESU). Trades a few
         cycles of cache-hit comparisons for elimination of an entire
         bug class.

    Either resolves the issue. Option 1 is more conservative; option 2 is
    simpler and matches how the new caching architecture wants to be used.

    **Audit**: while doing this, also grep for the dual triplet
    `_needs_redraw.add('list')` + `add('preview')` (only two; missing
    `'children'`) — that's the exact shape that regressed. Any current
    occurrence is suspicious.

    THE USER prefers to go with OPTION 1.

    * ## Comments {#223:comments}

      * Implemented Option 1: added mark_cursor_changed(browser) helper as a module-level function in 040-state.py (not 070-actions.py — placed there because cursor_to and _search_jump_nearest in 040 also need it; build-tui.sh concatenates files in numeric order so 070 can use 040 symbols, but not vice-versa). {#223:comment:235}

        Replaced 9 cursor-move triplet sites in 070-actions.py: _nav_down, _nav_up, _nav_home, _nav_end, _nav_pgdn, _nav_pgup, _nav_right (step-into-child), _nav_left (collapse + parent-jump), _search_next, _search_prev. Replaced 2 in 040-state.py: _search_jump_nearest, _do_cursor_to.
        Audit findings on the suspicious 'list'+'preview' (no 'children') dual-add pattern:
        1. _click_list_row in 070-actions.py (was line ~1492-1500) — moved state.cursor but only added 'list'. Confirmed bug shape (missing children + preview). Fixed by replacing with mark_cursor_changed.
        2. Search-mode key handler in dispatch_key (lines ~1026/1037/1047/1054) sets 'info'+'list' on each query keystroke — these don't move the cursor themselves; they update the query string and then call _search_jump_nearest, which now uses mark_cursor_changed. So these are intentional and not the bug shape.
        3. No other suspicious dual-add patterns remain. All remaining isolated 'preview'-only adds are tied to preview-scrolling or help-toggle, not cursor moves.
        Test wiring: added _actions.mark_cursor_changed = _state.mark_cursor_changed to 7 test files (test_actions, test_search, test_render_cache, test_help_text, test_scope_stack, test_main, test_multiselect, test_insert_mode).
        Tests: 937 passed, 4 skipped (unchanged from baseline). Build: clean.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Remove redundant explicit cache.prev_rect = cache.rect commits {#224}

        updated: 2026-05-07 00:26:26 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC

    **Severity**: low — cleanup / consistency. Not a bug today.

    **Issue**: several renderers explicitly commit `cache.prev_rect =
    cache.rect` at the end of their function bodies:
      - 050-render.py:1234 (`render_list`)
      - 050-render.py:1298, 1345 (`render_preview`, both early-return and
        end-of-function paths)
      - 050-render.py:1725, 1771 (`render_separator`, vertical-cached and
        horizontal-cached paths)
      - 050-render.py:1911 (`render_info_bar` use_cache path)

    These commits are redundant: `PaneCache.ensure` (040-state.py:148-169)
    already rolls `prev_rect` forward on the second paint via its `elif`
    branch:

        elif self.prev_rect != self.rect:
            self.prev_rect = self.rect

    `render_children_grid` and `render_children_list` correctly omit the
    explicit commit and rely on `ensure`. They work fine — coverage in
    test_render_cache.py confirms the steady-state cache-hit path is
    exercised for those panes.

    **Action**: pick one style and remove the duplication. The
    `ensure`-only style is preferred (centralizes lifecycle in one place).

    **Risk**: low. The two implementations are equivalent in current
    callers — both rotate prev_rect to rect on the second-paint
    transition. Removing the explicit commits should be a no-op behavior
    change covered by existing tests.

    **Why bother**: future maintainers reading the code see two ways to
    manage prev_rect and may pick wrong. Consolidating prevents that.

    * ## Comments {#224:comments}

      * Subsumed by #228 — the redesign centralizes cache lifecycle on PaneCache.update_rect() and includes this case in its acceptance criteria. Closing as wontfix; reopen if #228 ships without resolving it. {#224:comment:230}

  * ## Ticket: Task: render_info_bar emits redundant move/clear_line inside row capture {#225}

        updated: 2026-05-07 01:25:04 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC
        links: related:#228

    **Severity**: low — wasted bytes on every cache miss for the info bar.

    **Issue**: `render_info_bar` (050-render.py:1822) calls
    `move(row, 1)` and `clear_line()` unconditionally, even when running
    inside a `begin_row`/`end_row` capture (`use_cache=True` path).

    `begin_row` already records the (row, left) for `end_row` to emit as
    its leading `\e[<abs_row>;<left>H`. The inner `move(row, 1)` is
    captured into `_row_buf` and re-emitted on cache miss, producing
    output like:

        \e[24;1H\e[24;1H\e[2K<colored content>...

    The duplicated cursor-move is harmless (same position both times) but
    wasteful. Same shape exists in `render_separator`'s horizontal-cached
    path: the `if use_cache` branch correctly skips the explicit `move`,
    but the legacy non-cached path still calls `move` — so only one
    branch is "clean" today.

    **Fix**: in `render_info_bar`, gate the `move(row, 1)` and
    `clear_line()` calls behind `if not use_cache:`. The captured buffer
    doesn't need them — `begin_row` provides the position prefix and the
    pad/`\e[K` logic in `end_row` clears any stale cells.

    Note: removing `clear_line()` from the captured path requires
    verifying `end_row`'s pad/`\e[K` decision covers the cells previously
    cleared by `\e[2K`. The captured buffer's `_visible_len` would change
    (the `\e[2K` is currently stripped as a CSI), and the steady-state
    pad calculation depends on that count. Worth a careful unit test
    before merging.

    **Risk**: low if test coverage is added for the affected rows —
    test_render_cache.py already exercises the info-bar painting path.

    * ## Comments {#225:comments}

      * Independent of #228 (this is about move/clear_line emitted INTO the row buffer, not about cache lifecycle), but #228 touches the same renderer (render_info_bar) — natural moment to do them in the same PR if the author wants to bundle. {#225:comment:231}

      * Implemented: gated move(row, 1) + clear_line() behind 'if not use_cache:' in render_info_bar. begin_row/end_row already emit the position prefix, and end_row's pad/clear logic covers any cell-clearing the captured \e[2K used to do. Note: the visible_len of the info bar is always cols (the bar pads to full width with ─ glyphs), so end_row's shrink branch doesn't even need to fire in steady state — the new buffer simply overwrites the same cells the old one occupied. Added two regression tests in TestSeparatorCacheZeroBytes: (1) cache-miss paint contains exactly one cursor move and no \e[2K; (2) relabel repaint overwrites prior cells with no stale chars and no captured \e[2K, confirms cache stores visible_len == cols. All 939 tests pass; build succeeds. {#225:comment:236}

  * ## Ticket: Task: render_separator horizontal-cached path only paints row 0 {#226}

        updated: 2026-05-07 01:29:05 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC
        links: related:#228

    **Severity**: low — latent. No current caller triggers it.

    **Issue**: `render_separator` (050-render.py, horizontal cached
    branch around line 1737-1771) paints only `rel_row=0`:

        if use_cache:
            begin_row(cache, 0, rect.top, rect.left, rect.right, ...)
        ...
        if use_cache:
            end_row()
            cache.prev_rect = cache.rect

    But `cache.ensure(rect)` sized `cache.lines` to `rect.height`. If a
    caller passed `height > 1`, rows 1..n-1 would never be painted via
    the cache, and `end_row`'s cache-hit logic for those rows would
    short-circuit on `cached is None` checks (which is fine for emit
    decisions, but the rect-pad/clear logic for those rows is just
    skipped — no painting happens at all).

    **Why latent**: the docstring says "Horizontal — write on the first
    row of the rect (separators are 1-thick by construction; multi-row
    rects are clipped to the top row to keep the API forgiving)."
    Production code never passes a tall horizontal rect.

    **Fix options** (defensive):
      1. Loop `for rel_row in range(rect.height): begin_row(...); ...
         end_row()` so all rows participate in the cache and any future
         multi-row caller works correctly.
      2. Add an `assert rect.height == 1` (or coerce by clamping the
         rect) so the API contract is enforced rather than silently
         partial.

    Option 1 matches the vertical-cached branch's structure (which DOES
    loop). Option 2 is cheaper but kicks the can.

    The user prefers OPTION 1 since in future multi-line separators could be added.

    * ## Comments {#226:comments}

      * Independent of #228 (this is about painting all rows, not about cache lifecycle), but #228 touches the same renderer (render_separator) — natural moment to do them in the same PR if the author wants to bundle. {#226:comment:232}

      * Implemented option 1: looped begin_row/end_row over rect.height in the horizontal-cached branch of render_separator (mirrors the vertical-cached branch). The non-cached path also now loops for symmetry. Multi-row horizontal rects paint the bar glyphs on every row (consistent thicker bar). Added regression test test_horizontal_separator_multi_row_paints_every_row in TestSeparatorCacheZeroBytes that verifies (a) both rows of a height=2 rect emit 10 bar glyphs each on first paint, (b) cache.lines is fully populated, (c) second paint emits zero bytes. Full suite: 940 tests, all OK (4 skipped). Build clean. {#226:comment:237}

  * ## Ticket: Task: _handle_sigcont signal-safety: cross-reference Python signal semantics in docstring {#227}

        updated: 2026-05-07 01:32:09 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC

    **Severity**: note — documentation only. Not a bug today.

    **Issue**: `_handle_sigcont` (020-terminal.py:353) calls `_enter_raw()`,
    which writes via `sys.stdout.buffer.write(...)` and `flush()`. That's
    buffered I/O performed from a "signal handler".

    This is safe in Python because the interpreter only dispatches
    signals at bytecode boundaries (Python's signal handlers run between
    bytecodes, not inside arbitrary C calls), so there's no risk of
    re-entering stdio mid-write. But that's a non-obvious property — a
    future maintainer porting to a stricter signal-safety model (ctypes,
    asyncio integration, etc.) might break it.

    `_handle_sigtstp` already has a beautifully detailed docstring about
    the trailing-CALL-bytecode trick for SIGCONT delivery. `_handle_sigcont`
    itself is comparatively terse and doesn't mention why doing I/O here
    is OK.

    **Action**: add a one- or two-line comment in `_handle_sigcont`
    cross-referencing `_handle_sigtstp`'s docstring discussion of Python's
    bytecode-checkpoint signal dispatch, and noting that the buffered
    I/O is safe BECAUSE of that property (not in spite of it).

    **Pure documentation change, no behaviour change. No tests required.**

    * ## Comments {#227:comments}

      * Added a docstring note to _handle_sigcont in src-tui/020-terminal.py explaining that the buffered stdio in _enter_raw is safe BECAUSE Python dispatches signal handlers only at bytecode checkpoints (cross-references _handle_sigtstp's docstring for the full discussion), and flagging that future ports to stricter signal-safety regimes would need to revisit. build-tui.sh exit 0; run-tests.sh 940 tests OK (4 skipped). {#227:comment:238}

  * ## Ticket: Task: _visible_len counts code points instead of display columns {#222}

        updated: 2026-05-07 01:35:04 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-06 22:46:22 UTC

    **Severity**: low — latent bug, surfaces with non-ASCII content.

    **Location**: 020-terminal.py:140 (`_visible_len`).

    **Issue**: the function strips SGR sequences and increments `visible`
    once per remaining character (Python code point). It returns code-point
    count, not display-column count. CJK ideographs, most emoji, and some
    East Asian Ambiguous box-drawing glyphs render as 2 cells but count as
    1 here.

    **Why it matters**: the `end_row` steady-state padding path computes
    `pad = cached_visible - new_visible` (020-terminal.py:277). When the new
    content shrinks below the cached length, that many spaces are written
    to overwrite the trailing stale cells. If wide chars are involved, the
    visible_len under-counts → pad under-counts → trailing ghost characters
    remain on screen.

    Only triggers when ALL of:
      - row contains wide-cell characters,
      - new content is "shorter" than previous (in code-point count),
      - the pane is NOT rightmost (rightmost path uses `\e[K` and is immune).

    **Real-world impact**: most browse-tui usage is ASCII (filenames, plan
    ticket titles). Recipes that surface non-Latin titles — e.g.
    `browse-jira-mcp` with non-Latin tickets, or any recipe pulling
    user-supplied content with emoji — could see ghost characters on
    cursor moves.

    **Fix**: compute display-column width. Options:
      - `unicodedata.east_asian_width(ch) in ('W', 'F')` → 2, else 1.
        Stdlib only; covers CJK and Fullwidth. Misses some emoji.
      - Vendor a small wcwidth-style table for full coverage.

    **Test**: add a unit test in test_terminal_row_shim.py with a row that
    contains a CJK char (or `█` if you want to stay ASCII-adjacent) and
    shrinks, asserting the pad count is the column delta not the
    code-point delta.

    The user prefers going with OPTION 1 since it's the easiest to implement and it's an extremely rare case.

    * ## Comments {#222:comments}

      * Fixed _visible_len to use unicodedata.east_asian_width: chars with width 'W' or 'F' count as 2 cells, others as 1. SGR-skipping logic preserved. Added 5 new unit tests covering CJK ('東京'=4), mixed ('a東b'=4), ASCII no-regression, SGR stripping around wide char, and an end-to-end shrink scenario where '東京' shrinks to 'hi' in a non-rightmost pane (pad must be 2 cols, not 0). end_row pad math unchanged — both sides of the subtraction are now in display columns. Full test suite: 945 tests pass. {#222:comment:239}

* ## Ticket: Task: ANSI colors in preview pane {#240}

      updated: 2026-05-07 03:55:17 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-07 02:36:32 UTC

  ## Goal

  Render ANSI SGR colour codes in the preview pane. All other escape
  sequences are stripped. Default ON; toggle via CLI flag, Browser
  constructor argument, or capital-R hotkey.

  ## Design

  **Escape-sequence regex**: `\e\[[^a-zA-Z]*[a-zA-Z]` matches any CSI
  sequence. Sequences ending in `m` (SGR) are kept; everything else is
  dropped. Used for both rendering and width measurement (a single
  source of truth replaces the existing SGR-only strip in `_visible_len`).

  **Per-line wrap with colour preservation** via a small `SgrState`
  helper:

    * Walks the line emitting recognised SGR codes inline as it sees them.
    * Feeds the same SGR codes to `SgrState.feed()`.
    * At wrap boundaries: emits `\e[m`, yields the segment, then prefixes
      the next segment with `state.render()`.
    * End of line: emits trailing `\e[m` only if the line contained any
      SGR (so plain-text rows produce identical bytes regardless of
      ANSI mode — preserves cache hits).

  **First-iteration `SgrState`**: concatenates all fed codes verbatim;
  drops accumulated state on `\e[m` / `\e[0m`. Leaves a code-comment
  hook for a future improvement to track separate fg / bg / attrs
  slots and emit a minimal combined sequence on `render()`.

  **Search-highlight × ANSI collision**: when a preview line contains
  a search match, the walker runs in "strip all SGR" mode for that line
  — highlight wins. Documented in code; no special splicing.

  **Cache interaction**: no special handling. Toggling R changes the
  rendered bytes for colour-bearing rows → cache miss → redraw. Plain
  rows produce identical bytes either way → cache hit → no redraw.
  This naturally preserves the "minimum-bytes" invariant.

  **CLI / Browser / hotkey surface**:

    * `--preview-ansi` / `--no-preview-ansi` (argparse `BooleanOptionalAction`),
      default `True`.
    * `Browser(preview_ansi=True, ...)`.
    * Capital-R toggles `browser.preview_ansi` and flags `'preview'`
      for redraw.

  ## Tickets this depends on

  None — building on the post-#228 cache architecture.

  ## Out of scope

    * Tracking separate fg/bg/attrs slots in `SgrState` (future
      improvement; first iteration just concatenates).
    * Wide-char-aware wrapping (a separate latent bug; not blocked
      by this work; tracked under #222 already in production for
      `_visible_len`).
    * Preserving SGR through line-wrap when the search-highlight is
      present on the line (we drop source colours by design).

  * ## Ticket: Task: SgrState helper + ANSI regex primitive {#241}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-07 02:38:30 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-07 03:16:15 UTC

    **Severity**: foundation — blocks everything below.

    **Files**: `src-tui/020-terminal.py`, `test/unit/test_terminal_row_shim.py`.

    **What**:

      1. Add a module-level regex `_ANSI_CSI_RE = re.compile(r'\x1b\[[^a-zA-Z]*[a-zA-Z]')`
         near `_visible_len`. (The existing `_visible_len` regex strips
         only SGR; replace it with the broader CSI regex so cursor-move
         / erase / etc. embedded in content don't leak into width math.)

      2. Add a `SgrState` class:

         ```python
         class SgrState:
             """Accumulates SGR sequences seen in a stream; renders the active state.

             First iteration: concatenates all fed sequences verbatim, dropping
             on \\e[m / \\e[0m. Future improvement (TODO comment): track separate
             fg / bg / attrs slots so render() can emit a single minimal combined
             sequence (e.g. fg overwrite drops the previous fg code).
             """

             def __init__(self):
                 self._buf = ''  # concatenated SGR sequences seen since last reset

             def feed(self, sgr_seq: str) -> None:
                 """Apply one '\\e[...m' sequence. '\\e[m' or '\\e[0m' clears."""
                 # Reset detection: empty params or single '0'.

             def render(self) -> str:
                 """Return the active state as bytes (or '' if empty)."""
                 return self._buf

             def is_empty(self) -> bool:
                 return not self._buf

             def reset(self) -> None:
                 self._buf = ''
         ```

      3. Update `_visible_len` to use `_ANSI_CSI_RE` (not the SGR-only
         version). Keep the wide-char column counting from #222.

    **Tests** (`test_terminal_row_shim.py`):

      * `_visible_len` now strips non-SGR CSI too: `_visible_len('\\e[2Jhello') == 5`.
      * `SgrState.feed('\\e[31m')` then `.render() == '\\e[31m'`.
      * `feed('\\e[31m')` + `feed('\\e[1m')` then `render() == '\\e[31m\\e[1m'`
        (concat — first iteration explicitly does NOT collapse).
      * `feed('\\e[31m')` + `feed('\\e[m')` then `render() == ''` (reset clears).
      * `feed('\\e[31m')` + `feed('\\e[0m')` then `render() == ''` (also reset).
      * `is_empty()` round-trips with the above.
      * Regression: existing `_visible_len` tests for SGR stripping + wide
        chars still pass (the regex generalisation must not break them).

    * ## Comments {#241:comments}

      * Implemented _ANSI_CSI_RE regex, SgrState class, and refactored _visible_len to use the broader CSI regex. Added 9 new tests (2 visible_len, 7 SgrState). All 956 tests pass; build succeeds. {#241:comment:248}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Preview-line walker with wrap-aware SGR re-emit {#242}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-07 02:38:30 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-07 03:23:46 UTC

    **Files**: `src-tui/050-render.py`, `test/unit/test_render.py` or new
    `test/unit/test_preview_ansi.py`.

    **What**: a helper that consumes one logical preview line + a target
    width and yields self-contained visual rows, preserving SGR through
    wrap boundaries. Replaces the current naive `while len(line) > width: ...`
    slice in `render_preview` (around 050-render.py:1322).

    ```python
    def _wrap_preview_line(line: str, width: int, *, ansi_on: bool,
                           drop_sgr: bool = False) -> list[str]:
        """Wrap a logical preview line into visual rows of <= ``width`` cols.

        ``ansi_on``  — keep SGR codes inline. False → strip all CSI (raw mode).
        ``drop_sgr`` — strip all SGR even in ANSI mode (used when a line
                       contains a search highlight; highlight wins).

        Each yielded row is self-contained: any active SGR is re-emitted at
        its start, and a trailing ``\\e[m`` is appended iff the row contains
        any SGR. Plain rows produce identical bytes whether ``ansi_on`` is
        True or False — preserves cache-hit invariants.
        """
    ```

    ## Algorithm: regex-tokenised, ASCII-fast

    **Step 1 — tokenise.** Single `_ANSI_CSI_RE.finditer` pass; yield
    alternating `('text', s)` / `('csi', s)` tokens:

    ```python
    def _tokenise_line(line):
        pos = 0
        for m in _ANSI_CSI_RE.finditer(line):
            if m.start() > pos:
                yield ('text', line[pos:m.start()])
            yield ('csi', m.group(0))
            pos = m.end()
        if pos < len(line):
            yield ('text', line[pos:])
    ```

    **Step 2 — process tokens.**

      * For `csi` tokens: if it ends in `'m'` and `ansi_on` and
        `not drop_sgr` → emit inline + `state.feed(tok)`. Otherwise drop.
      * For `text` tokens: walk in chunks (NOT char-by-char in the
        common case). Three-tier fast path:

    ```python
    i = 0
    token_is_ascii = tok.isascii()  # O(1) flag check, computed once per token

    while i < len(tok):
        avail = width - seg_vis
        if avail <= 0:
            end_row()
            continue

        end = min(i + avail, len(tok))

        # Fast path 1: whole token is ASCII → every cut is ASCII.
        # Fast path 2: this particular cut is ASCII (wide chars lie further in).
        if token_is_ascii or tok[i:end].isascii():
            seg.append(tok[i:end])
            seg_vis += end - i        # ASCII ⇒ chars == cols
            i = end
        else:
            # Slow path: wide chars in this cut. Char-by-char column fit.
            j, taken = i, 0
            while j < end:
                w = _char_width(tok[j])
                if taken + w > avail:
                    break
                taken += w
                j += 1
            if j == i:                    # single wide char into empty avail
                j, taken = i + 1, _char_width(tok[i])
            seg.append(tok[i:j])
            seg_vis += taken
            i = j

        if seg_vis >= width:
            end_row()
    ```

    **Step 3 — `end_row` helper.** Closes the current segment with
    `\e[m` iff state non-empty, yields the joined string, then opens
    the next segment by re-emitting `state.render()` (only if non-empty).
    Resets `seg_vis = 0`.

    **Step 4 — flush.** After the token loop, emit the final row
    (always emit at least one row, even for an empty input line).

    ## Why this shape

      * **Block-by-block, not char-by-char.** Escape sequences are
        identified as single units by the regex; we never scan looking
        for `\e` per char.
      * **ASCII fast path is the common case.** `_str_width` /
        `_char_width` (which call `unicodedata.east_asian_width`) are
        reserved for cuts that actually contain wide chars.
      * **Per-cut ASCII discrimination.** A token like
        `"hello world ... 東京"` with the wide chars near the end takes
        fast path 2 for every wrap segment that doesn't straddle the
        wide chars; only the segment that does falls through to the
        char loop.

    ## Tests

    Cover all three paths plus the ANSI semantics:

      * Plain ASCII line wraps identically to the old slice path
        (regression).
      * Coloured line wider than width: wrap segments each carry the
        active SGR + trailing `\e[m`.
      * Reset mid-line: subsequent wrap segments drop the colour
        (`\e[m` clears `SgrState`).
      * `\e[2J` (non-SGR CSI) embedded in content: stripped, doesn't
        count toward width.
      * `ansi_on=False`: all CSI stripped; output indistinguishable
        from pre-ANSI behaviour.
      * `drop_sgr=True`: SGR codes stripped even in ANSI mode
        (highlight path).
      * Empty line yields one empty row.
      * Line of exactly `width` cols yields one row, no wrap.
      * **Fast-path coverage**:
        - All-ASCII token (whole-token fast path).
        - Mixed token where the cut is ASCII but the rest isn't
          (per-cut fast path).
        - Mixed token where the cut contains wide chars (slow path).
      * **Wide-char wrap** (CJK content):
        - Single CJK char doesn't fit in remaining cols → ends the
          current row, lands on the next.
        - Slow-path under-fill is correct (`avail=5`, `"a東b"` cut →
          emits 4 cols, leaves 1 col on the floor as designed).

    * ## Comments {#242:comments}

      * Implemented _wrap_preview_line + _tokenise_line in 050-render.py (placed just before render_preview), added shared _char_width helper to 020-terminal.py next to _visible_len. New test file test/unit/test_preview_ansi.py covers tokeniser, plain ASCII regression vs slice path, coloured wrap with SGR re-emit, mid-row reset, non-SGR CSI strip, ansi_on=False, drop_sgr=True, all three fast-path tiers, and CJK wrap edge cases (under-fill, single-char-into-width-1). Refinement vs spec: trailing \e[m only emitted when state is non-empty at end of row (cleaner than 'any SGR in row' — avoids redundant resets after explicit mid-row reset). Suppressed dangling SGR-only flush row when input ends exactly on a wrap boundary. 27 new tests pass; full suite 983 tests OK; build-tui.sh produces valid concatenated output. Wiring into render_preview is deferred to #243. {#242:comment:249}

  * ## Ticket: End-to-end UI test (tmux): R hotkey toggles preview rendering {#246}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-07 02:38:30 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-07 03:49:42 UTC

    **Files**: new `test/ui/test_preview_ansi.py` + recipe.

    **What**: drive a real terminal session through tmux and assert:

      1. With ANSI on (default), a preview containing `\\e[31mhello\\e[m`
         displays "hello" with red foreground (capture the SGR codes from
         the tmux pane).
      2. Pressing capital-R: the next paint shows the same text without
         SGR codes.
      3. Pressing R again: SGR codes return.
      4. The cursor-position rows that don't contain colours don't get
         redrawn on the toggle (cache hit invariant).

    Optional: also assert `--no-preview-ansi` startup path matches the
    toggled-off state.

* ## Ticket: Task: browse-claude: rich previews for sessions and messages {#255}

      updated: 2026-05-07 04:35:27 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-07 04:21:12 UTC

  Make per-line and per-session previews structure-aware in recipes/browse-claude.
  Today _preview_message returns json.dumps and _preview_session dumps raw lines.

  Approach (agreed in chat):
  - Keep recipe single-file. ~+450 lines, no abstractions, no semantic helpers.
  - ANSI color constants at top of file; _init_color() zeros them when NO_COLOR / non-tty.
  - Renderers are flat free functions. Each takes obj, returns str. They splice ANSI directly via f-strings (e.g. f'{GREEN}+ {line}{RESET}').
  - _classify(obj) maps a parsed JSONL record to a renderer key.
  - _RENDERERS dict dispatches; unknown keys fall back to today's pretty-JSON (forward-compat).

  Replaceability levers: change palette constants → re-theme; change a kind→COLOR dict → change accents; add a new type → write _render_X, register in _RENDERERS + _classify.

  Subtasks #256–#258 land in order; recipe stays runnable after each.

* ## Ticket: Task: Public thread-safe Browser API: reorganise + add set_children / set_preview {#265}

      updated: 2026-05-08 01:40:01 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-08 00:58:46 UTC

  ## Goal

  Recipes that run their own background threads (asyncio bridges, IPC
  daemons, native worker pools) need a clear, documented set of
  Browser methods they can call from any thread. The block already
  exists at `040-state.py:1066` but has gaps and inconsistencies.
  This ticket tightens it.

  ## Changes

  ### 1. Make `set_list_ratio` and `set_split` thread-safe

  Current: directly mutates `self.list_ratio` / `self.split` and
  `_needs_redraw`. Race with the renderer.

  Fix: wrap each in `post(...)` calling a `_do_set_list_ratio` /
  `_do_set_split` private method that does the actual mutation on
  the main thread.

  ### 2. Move `watch` out of the block

  `watch` is a registration helper called during construction; it's
  not thread-safe and isn't a runtime API. Relocate before the block
  banner (below `extend_actions` is a natural home — both are
  construction-time helpers).

  ### 3. Add `set_children(id_, items)`

  Formal version of `_children_results.append(...)`. Lets recipes
  with their own children-fetching threads deliver results without
  using the built-in worker pool.

  ```python
  def set_children(self, id_, items):
      """(thread-safe) Inject pre-fetched children for ``id_`` from any thread.

      Equivalent to what the built-in children worker does after a
      successful fetch — but lets recipe-owned threads (any threading
      model: native threads, asyncio bridges, IPC daemons) deliver
      results without going through ``request_children``. Items are
      coerced via ``to_item`` so the recipe can pass plain dicts.

      A recipe that manages all fetching itself can pass
      ``get_children=None`` to disable the built-in worker.
      """
      coerced = [to_item(x) for x in items]
      self._children_results.append((id_, coerced))
      notify_wake()
  ```

  ### 4. Add `set_preview(id_, text)`

  Sibling of `set_children`. Writes to the latest-wins preview-result
  slot. Recipes using this should pass `get_preview=None` to avoid
  racing with the built-in `_preview_worker`.

  ```python
  def set_preview(self, id_, text):
      """(thread-safe) Inject pre-fetched preview text for ``id_`` from any thread.

      Latest-wins: a later ``set_preview`` overwrites an unconsumed
      earlier one. Recipes using this should construct the Browser
      with ``get_preview=None`` so the built-in worker doesn't race.
      ``text`` is coerced to ``''`` if None.
      """
      if text is None:
          text = ''
      self._preview_result = (id_, text)
      notify_wake()
  ```

  ### 5. Reorganise as a banner-bracketed block

  Replace the current `# ---- public, thread-safe API ----` line
  with a prominent multi-line banner that lists every member and
  closes with an explicit end marker:

  ```python
  # =========================================================================
  # Public, thread-safe API
  # =========================================================================
  # Every method in this block is safe to call from any thread.
  # Mutations are deferred to the main loop's drain via post(),
  # the children-results deque, or the preview-result slot.
  #
  #   post(fn)                    — schedule fn() on the next main-thread drain
  #   message(text) / error(text) — surface a status / error
  #   refresh(id)                 — schedule re-fetch of children
  #   cursor_to(id)               — move cursor (expanding ancestors)
  #   expand(id)                  — expand a parent (and fetch if needed)
  #   set_children(id, items)     — inject pre-fetched children
  #   set_preview(id, text)       — inject pre-fetched preview text
  #   set_list_ratio(ratio)       — resize the list pane
  #   set_split(s)                — change the split layout
  #   select(ids, replace=False)  — set the multi-select set
  #   cancel(*pendings)           — cancel one or more Pending handles
  #   quit(code=0, output='')     — exit the run loop
  #
  # Methods OUTSIDE this block are main-thread-only.
  # =========================================================================
  ```

  And close with:

  ```python
  # =========================================================================
  # End of public, thread-safe API
  # =========================================================================
  ```

  ### 6. Tag every method's docstring

  Open every docstring in the block with the `(thread-safe)` tag on
  its first line so `help(Browser.message)` makes the contract
  obvious in isolation:

  ```python
  def message(self, text):
      """(thread-safe) Surface ``text`` as a transient status message.

      ...
      """
  ```

  Existing methods that already say "Safe to call from any thread"
  get the tag and the prose can stay (or be condensed).

  ## Tests

  * `Browser.set_children(id_, items)`:
    - From a worker thread, items appear in the next `apply_children_results` drain.
    - Items can be plain dicts; `to_item` coercion happens inside.
    - Multiple calls from different threads queue FIFO.
  * `Browser.set_preview(id_, text)`:
    - From a worker thread, text appears in the next preview drain.
    - Latest-wins: a second call overwrites the first if not yet consumed.
    - `None` is coerced to `''`.
  * `Browser.set_split(s)`, `Browser.set_list_ratio(r)`:
    - Calling from a worker thread doesn't directly mutate state until
      the main loop drains. (Schedule, drain, observe.)
    - Existing in-tree usage (if any) still works after the wrap.
  * `watch` is no longer in the thread-safe block — verify by reading
    the source structure (no runtime test needed; this is a layout
    change).

  ## Out of scope

  * Concurrency-stress tests — single-thread queue drain semantics
    are already covered by existing tests.
  * Renaming any existing method to add a `post_` / `safe_` prefix
    — explicitly rejected after design discussion (block banner +
    docstring tags provide the visibility without the breaking
    rename or the post-routing misnomer for non-post-routed
    members).

    * ## Comments {#270:comments}

      * Implemented Context push surface (#270). {#270:comment:281}

        Files changed:
        - src-tui/040-state.py: added Browser.append_preview, Browser.clear_preview (set_preview already existed from #265).
        - src-tui/060-context.py: added ctx.update_data, ctx.upsert, ctx.set_item, ctx.remove, ctx.set_preview, ctx.append_preview, ctx.clear_preview, ctx.run_in_worker.
        - test/unit/test_context_push.py: 29 new tests covering forwarding, return values, exception handling, and end-to-end state mutation.
        Preview cache shape: _state._preview is a per-id dict (item_id -> text), so per-id append/clear is naturally well-defined. Spec aligns with existing shape; no design wrinkle.
        Routing decisions documented inline:
        - set_preview routes via the existing _preview_result single-slot worker pipeline (untouched, preserves #265 contract and tests).
        - append_preview / clear_preview route via post() to mutate _state._preview on the main thread directly (read-modify-write needs to be atomic w.r.t. renderer / worker, post() is the cleanest path; the slot can't represent appends or deletions).
        - run_in_worker spawns a fresh daemon thread (matches Browser.watch's pattern); existing _children_worker is a parent-id FIFO, not a callable runner, so reusing it would conflate unrelated traffic.
        Documented in code: the ordering caveat between set_preview (slot path, drained AFTER post queue via apply_preview_result) and append_preview/clear_preview (post path). Recipes that need strict ordering should pick one path per id. Acceptable trade-off given the realistic usage shape.
        Test totals: 1216 unit tests, 4 skipped, 0 failures. New file adds 29 tests.

        updated: 2026-05-08 08:50:45 UTC

    Children worker builds an `update_data` batch (upserts + trailing
    `complete(parent_id)` op) and calls `browser.update_data(batch)`. `_loading`
    is set on the main thread when the worker is dispatched. `None` return
    posts no batch; loading stays.

    - All existing `get_children` tests pass with no test-code changes.
    - New test: a watcher push that arrives during a `get_children` call ends up
      in the cache alongside the return value (both visible, no loss — the
      documented behavioural change from clobber to append).
    - Empty list return → batch of just `[complete(parent_id)]`.

    * ## Comments {#271:comments}

      * Done. Worker now delivers via `update_data` (#268 ops) instead of the {#271:comment:285}

        legacy `_children_results` deque.
        What changed:
        - `_children_worker` (040-state.py): user_fn return is coerced via
          `to_item`; iterable returns build a batch
          `[upsert(id, parent, **fields_of(item)) for items] + [complete(parent)]`
          and call `browser.update_data(batch)`. None returns post nothing
          (loading stays True). Errors caught at the boundary still synthesise
          an empty delivery so the placeholder clears.
        - New helpers: `_fields_of_item(item)` (uses `__dict__`, excludes id)
          and `_build_children_batch(parent_id, items)` near the apply_ops
          helpers.
        - New main-thread callable `Browser._post_children_delivery(parent_id)`:
          posted by the worker AFTER `update_data` so apply_ops has run by
          the time it fires. Three jobs:
            1. `_children.setdefault(parent, [])` — ensures cache entry exists
               (visible builder distinguishes absent → placeholder vs empty
               list → render nothing). Without this, an empty return after
               `cache_invalidate_subtree` would leave a placeholder dangling.
            2. Discard `_children_pending`.
            3. Resolve every Pending in `_children_in_flight[parent]`.
          Also clamps cursor (#125 regression guard) and flags list/children/all
          for redraw.
        Pending integration: queue.Queue is FIFO, so two posts in order
        (`update_data` then `_post_children_delivery`) drain in order on the
        main thread. `then` callbacks observe the post-batch state.
        Design call (small one): `_apply_upsert` previously silent-dropped
        new ids with `parent_id=None`. That semantics is needed for patch-only
        of unknown ids (per spec Section 2). But it also broke the worker
        delivery path for `root_id=None` Browsers (the framework default,
        used by many tests). I disambiguated: silent-drop only when
        `state.root_id is not None`. When `root_id is None`, parent_id=None
        *is* the root, so the upsert inserts. The existing test
        `test_patch_only_unknown_id_silent_drop` uses `State(root_id='/')`
        and still passes; the change only affects the rare case where
        someone explicitly uses `root_id=None` AND patches an unknown id —
        they now get an insert under None instead of a drop. Documented
        inline in `_apply_upsert`.
        Kept: `_children_results` deque + `apply_children_results` are
        preserved as the thin shim path for `set_children` (replace
        semantics, used by recipes that bypass the worker). Worker no
        longer touches the deque.
        Tests: added test/async_/test_children_delivery.py with 13 tests
        covering empty list, None, mixed shapes (Item/str/tuple/dict),
        custom-attr round-trip, pending fires-after-apply (cache + indexes
        + loading), watcher-during-fetch (both orderings), and a regression
        guard that worker no longer enqueues to the legacy deque.
        Test count: 1216 → 1229 (all pass). No existing test code modified.

  * ## Ticket: Preview generator: buffered eager-pull + cursor-move abandon {#273}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-08 07:20:36 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-08 09:13:20 UTC

    `get_preview` accepts generators. Preview worker eagerly pulls, calling
    `browser.append_preview(item_id, chunk)` per yield, until a configurable
    buffer cap. Pause until cursor-move abandon (or demand signal — next ticket).

    - Generator return path coexists with today's str-return path.
    - Cap default ~1000 lines or ~100 KB, configurable.
    - Cursor-move stops the worker pulling; generator goes out of scope;
      recipe `finally` block fires.
    - Tests cover: streaming yields, cap-then-pause, abandon-mid-stream,
      `finally`-fires-on-abandon.

    * ## Comments {#273:comments}

      * Implemented preview generator support in src-tui/040-state.py. {#273:comment:287}

        Cap config surface: Browser kwargs preview_buffer_cap_chars (default 100_000) + preview_buffer_cap_lines (default 1000). Whichever cap hits first triggers pause. Stored as self._preview_buffer_cap_{chars,lines}.
        Pause-state location: self._preview_paused on Browser (None or dict {id, gen, chars, lines}), guarded by new self._preview_lock. Lives next to existing _preview_req/_preview_result/_preview_event.
        Cursor-move signal mechanism: reused the existing _preview_req slot the worker already polls. The pause-wait loop checks 'self._preview_req != item_id' on each wake — covers both 'a different id was requested' and 'cursor moved off any item' (sets _preview_req=None). Added a new _preview_resume_event (threading.Event) purely as the wake mechanism for the in-pause wait. Set by request_preview, by cursor-off-item path in _update_preview_for_cursor, and by stop_workers. The worker also wakes via 0.5s wait timeout as a safety net.
        Outer worker calls _abandon_paused_preview_if_any(except_id=req_id) before serving each new request — guarantees the recipe's finally fires before pivoting. The streaming branch ALSO closes its own gen on cursor-move (whichever observes it first; the other path no-ops via the still_paused guard).
        Design calls:
        * When entering pause, leave _preview_req == item_id (don't clear). Cleaner abandon semantics; the pause-wait loop directly observes any change. To keep run_until_idle from hanging, extended it to recognise the paused state as 'idle'.
        * StopIteration clears _preview_req and exits without auto-clearing the buffered preview (the buffer IS the final preview, per ticket).
        * Mid-stream exception appends '[error] X: msg' to the buffer (so user sees partial + error tag) and exits. Initial-call exception still uses legacy str-error path via _preview_result for parity with non-generator code path.
        * TODO #274 markers left in _stream_preview_from_generator at the resume signal point.
        * Non-string yields coerced via str() (None becomes '').
        Added test/async_/test_preview_generator.py (16 tests) covering: streaming yields, intermediate visibility between yields, non-str chunk coercion, chars-cap pause + no-further-pulls, lines-cap pause, cursor-move abandon (paused / cursor-off-item / mid-stream-pre-pause), string return regression, None return regression, mixed string+generator returns, mid-stream exception (partial buffer + error tag), initial-call exception, supersede-paused-with-new-request, empty generator, clean-exhaustion clears request slot.
        Build: ./build-tui.sh OK. Tests: ./run-tests.sh — 1263 passed (1247 existing + 16 new), 4 skipped, 0 failed.

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-08 07:20:36 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-08 09:29:25 UTC

    Renderer detects preview scroll within N rows of the buffered tail and
    signals the preview worker to resume pulling from the paused generator.
    Worker resumes; pulls until cap again; pauses.

    - Scrolling near the buffered end resumes pulling.
    - Scrolling back / cursor moving away does not.
    - UI test covers scroll-driven resume.

    * ## Comments {#274:comments}

      * Implemented renderer demand-signal + worker resume for paused preview generators. {#274:comment:288}

        Threshold: 12 wrapped rows (constant _PREVIEW_DEMAND_THRESHOLD in 050-render.py).
        Renderer fires when total_buffered_lines - visible_end_row < threshold AND a generator is paused for the cursored id.
        Debounce: Browser._preview_demand_signal_state holds (id, scroll) of the last fire; renderer skips when unchanged. Reset on every new pause cycle so the next viewport-near-tail render after re-pause re-fires.
        Design calls:
          * New Browser._preview_resume_pull bool + Browser.signal_preview_demand(item_id) public method. Distinguishes resume from abandon inside the pause-wait loop without needing a sentinel value in _preview_paused.
          * Pause-wait loop: on wake checks _preview_resume_pull under _preview_lock. If True, clears paused state + flag, breaks back to outer pull loop. Cursor-move check stays first.
          * Cap counters become cumulative (next_cap_chars/next_cap_lines advanced by one cap window per resume) so _preview_paused['chars'] retains the running-total semantics #273 documented.
          * _abandon_paused_preview_if_any + finally-block clear the resume-pull flag too — no stale signals across generators.
        Files changed:
          src-tui/040-state.py — flag/state init, signal_preview_demand, pause-wait resume branch, cumulative cap.
          src-tui/050-render.py — _PREVIEW_DEMAND_THRESHOLD constant + demand-detect block in render_preview.
          test/async_/test_preview_resume.py — 8 tests (resume cycles, no-op cases, cursor-move during resume, exhaustion, idle).
          test/ui/test_preview_resume.py + test/ui/recipes/preview_resume.py — UI test scrolls past initial cap until LINE_100 / LINE_200 appear via demand-resume.

    * ## Ticket: Task: Fix update_data to trigger redraw {#290}

          updated: 2026-05-08 09:48:11 UTC
          status: done
          created: 2026-05-08 09:43:34 UTC

      update_data posts apply_ops which flips _visible_dirty but the main loop only renders when _needs_redraw has entries. So a watcher pushing pure update_data ops doesn't cause a re-render until the user presses a key. Streaming-push spec line 107 says 'one render afterward'. Fix: make update_data's posted callable also add 'list'/'children'/'all' to _needs_redraw after apply_ops returns. Discovered while writing #276 watcher UI test.

      * ## Comments {#290:comments}

        * Fixed by extending Browser.update_data's posted callable to flag _needs_redraw['list'] and ['children'] after apply_ops returns. Without this the main loop would only repaint after the next keystroke, breaking the spec's 'one render afterward' contract for any pure update_data path (watchers, websocket bridges). Children-worker delivery already covered redraw via _post_children_delivery; only the watcher path was affected. {#290:comment:291}

* ## Ticket: Task: Full refresh strands expanded sub-trees in loading state {#294}

      updated: 2026-05-11 03:53:01 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-11 03:50:01 UTC

  **Repro.** Build a tree where `/a → /a/b → /a/b/c` are all expanded; cursor on
  `/a/b/c` (or any deep descendant). Press `Ctrl-R` (full refresh). The expanded
  sub-parents render `⧗ loading…` placeholders that never resolve until the
  user moves the cursor onto each parent in turn.

  **Root cause.** `Browser._do_refresh(None, pending)` calls
  `cache_invalidate_all` (clears `_children` for every parent) but only
  enqueues a fetch for `state.root_id`. Expanded sub-parents lose their
  children entries with no re-dispatch attached. The visible-tree builder
  emits a placeholder for any expanded parent missing from `_children` but
  never kicks the worker. The only auto-dispatch is `_update_children_for_cursor`,
  which fires for the cursor item only.

  **Fix.** Snapshot `state.expanded` (and the current scope root) before
  `cache_invalidate_all`; enqueue dispatches for each in addition to
  `state.root_id`. Partial refresh path (`_do_refresh(specific_id, …)`) stays
  as-is — that contract is "re-fetch this id's children" and grandchildren
  caches survive.

  - Add a failing async test covering the full-refresh-while-deep-cursor scenario:
    expanded chain, cursor deep, refresh full, run_until_idle, assert every
    previously-expanded parent was re-fetched (children present in `_children`,
    `_loading[parent]=False`).
  - Implement the snapshot + multi-dispatch in `_do_refresh`.
  - Verify existing tests pass.

  * ## Comments {#294:comments}

    * Root cause: _do_refresh(None) cleared all caches via cache_invalidate_all but only enqueued a fetch for state.root_id. Expanded sub-parents lost their _children entries with no re-dispatch attached. Fixed by snapshotting state.expanded (plus the current scope root) before invalidation and enqueueing fetches for each. Partial refresh path unchanged. +3 tests; 1281 → 1284, all pass. {#294:comment:295}

* ## Ticket: browse-plan: push patches via update_data instead of full refresh {#296}

      updated: 2026-05-11 05:19:33 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-11 05:16:47 UTC

  Three action handlers — `_action_status`, `_action_close`, `_action_reopen` —
  call `ctx.refresh()` after a successful `plan` mutation, forcing a full
  re-fetch of the current scope. Loses expansion state, re-shells out to
  `plan list`, rebuilds the visible tree — for what's a one-row update.

  Replace with targeted `ctx.update_data([upsert(id, None, tag=NEW,
  tag_style=…)])` batches. Patch-merge semantics preserve cursor + expansion.

  - `_action_status`: patch `tag` and `tag_style` to the chosen status.
  - `_action_close`: `plan IDS close` sets status to `done`; patch to that.
  - `_action_reopen`: `plan IDS reopen` sets status to `open`; patch to that.

  Leave `_action_edit`, `_action_create`, `_action_move` calling
  `ctx.refresh()` — those can change shape (title/body/children/parent/order)
  in ways `upsert(id, None, …)` alone can't express. Document the asymmetry.

  Done when:
  - The three handlers push `update_data` patches instead of refresh.
  - Existing UI test `test_status_picker_changes_status` still passes.
  - Manual smoke: status change does NOT collapse expansion below the row.

  * ## Comments {#296:comments}

    * Converted _action_status, _action_close, _action_reopen to push upsert(id, None, ...) patches via ctx.update_data. _action_edit, _action_create, _action_move kept on ctx.refresh() — those mutations change shape in ways upsert(id, None, ...) alone can't express. Existing UI test_status_picker_changes_status passes; full suite 1284/1284. {#296:comment:297}

* ## Ticket: Task: browse-claude: tree view mode {#298}

      updated: 2026-05-14 01:46:04 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-14 01:30:36 UTC

  Tree mode for browse-claude.

  Settled in chat:
  - One recipe, flat & tree coexist. CLI: --tree / --no-tree (default flat). Runtime toggle: 't'.
  - Tree only changes within-session listings. Project/session level identical.
  - Sessions still sort newest-first by mtime; messages inside a session in tree mode go in file order.
  - Cap removed in tree mode (full file scan needed).
  - parentUuid is the wire; inheritedPromptId = node's promptId OR parent's. Break parent link when child's inheritedPromptId ≠ parent's → that child becomes a turn-root.
  - Metadata records (no parentUuid) are roots at their file position.
  - Orphans (parentUuid doesn't resolve) → roots, mark node.orphan = True.
  - Subagents wired into tree as a child of the **assistant row** carrying the Agent/Task tool_use. Represented as one collapsible row using the existing #agent:<id> id shape. Default collapsed.
  - All subtrees collapsed by default.
  - On open / drill-in / t-toggle: cursor lands on latest voice; viewport scrolls. Walk parentUuid chain to expand ancestors when needed (cursor_to is best-effort if not visible).
  - Tree indent uses the framework's ▶/▼ + 2-space-per-level mechanism. No └─ in titles. └ OK as a marker icon for subagent rows.
  - Glyphs: match Claude Code (⏺ assistant, ⑂ fork) where they exist; keep our 🔧 etc. otherwise.

  Subtickets:
  #299 — tree builder + caching + node attrs
  #300 — get_children dispatch
  #301 — cursor + t toggle + CLI
  #302 — polish, glyphs, tests

  * ## Ticket: Task: Tree builder: scan + cache + node attrs (parentUuid map, inheritedPromptId, orphan/meta/turn_root) {#299}

        updated: 2026-05-14 01:34:24 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-14 01:30:49 UTC

    Add _scan_tree(jsonl_path) returning a cached struct keyed by mtime:

      records:       list of parsed JSON objects in file order (line index aligned).
      by_uuid:       {uuid: record}
      by_parent:     {parentUuid: [records sorted by file position]}, None key for roots.
      inherited_pid: {uuid: promptId-from-self-or-ancestor} — propagate down parentUuid chain.
      roots:         records that act as tree roots:
                       * parentUuid is None
                       * parentUuid doesn't resolve (orphan — flag node.orphan=True)
                       * inheritedPromptId differs from parent's (turn-root — flag node.is_turn_root=True)
                       * metadata-type records with no parentUuid field (flag node.is_meta=True)
                       * forkedFrom set (flag node.forked_from=value)
      agent_link:    for each tool_result record whose toolUseResult.agentId resolves to a sibling
                     subagent .jsonl in <session_id>/subagents/, store {tool_use_id, agent_id, agent_path}.
                     This drives the 'subagent under the assistant row' wiring at the get_children layer.

    Cache invalidation: keyed by (path, mtime). Re-scan on mtime change.

    Node attrs land on the existing message Item (built by _list_messages in flat mode, or a tree-mode equivalent in #300). Both modes can read these attrs — tree mode uses them for structure, flat mode can use orphan/forked_from for visual marks if it wants.

    Unit tests (test/unit/test_browse_claude_render.py):
    - inheritedPromptId propagates through the chain on a fixture with user→asst→asst→user (new promptId).
    - Multi-turn fixture: each new user's parent (last asst of prev turn) is detected as a turn boundary.
    - Orphan: synthesise a record with parentUuid pointing nowhere; flagged orphan=True.
    - forkedFrom propagates to node attr.
    - Cache invalidates when mtime changes.

  * ## Ticket: Task: get_children dispatch: tree-mode listings (root level, parent->children, subagent under assistant row) {#300}

        updated: 2026-05-14 01:37:18 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-14 01:30:49 UTC

    Wire the tree builder into the recipe's get_children:

    Tree mode dispatch (when _TREE_MODE is True):
      id = <jsonl>           → root-level nodes in file order. Includes turn-roots, orphans, and metadata records, intermixed by position.
      id = <jsonl>#<n>       → children of that record:
                                (a) records whose parentUuid==record.uuid AND inheritedPromptId matches.
                                    (Children with a DIFFERENT inheritedPromptId belong to a new turn-root — DON'T list them under this record.)
                                (b) if this record is an assistant message containing an Agent/Task tool_use, attach a
                                    pseudo-child Item with id <jsonl>#agent:<agentId> (using existing shape). This is the
                                    collapsible subagent row.
      id = <sess>#agent:<aid> → root-level nodes of the subagent .jsonl, again in tree shape (recurse via _scan_tree).
      Other ids                → same as flat mode (project / session listings unchanged).

    Each tree-mode message Item gets has_children=True when children-by-parent is non-empty OR when it carries a subagent attach. Otherwise False (renders without the ▶/▼ marker).

    Don't change _summarise_message titles — same per-record one-liners. Order children by file position (parent appears first in file, children appear after).

    Flat mode (when _TREE_MODE is False): no change. Existing _list_messages window still applies.

    Unit tests:
    - Root-level list for a fixture session: turn boundaries become roots; metadata interleaved at their positions.
    - Drill into a turn root → see its assistant + tool_result descendants; new-turn user is NOT listed here.
    - Assistant row with Agent tool_use surfaces both the tool_result and the #agent:<id> pseudo-child.
    - Subagent's own .jsonl renders with its own tree (recursive call works).

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cursor-on-open + t toggle + --tree/--no-tree CLI; walk-up-and-expand for cursor preservation {#301}

        updated: 2026-05-14 01:41:28 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-14 01:30:49 UTC

    Three wires:

    1. CLI flags: --tree / --no-tree, mutually exclusive. Set the module-level _TREE_MODE bool before Browser() is constructed. Help text updated.

    2. 't' action (Action('t', 'Toggle flat / tree view', _action_toggle_tree, 'none')):
       - Capture cursor's item.id BEFORE flipping.
       - Flip _TREE_MODE.
       - ctx.refresh() to invalidate cached children across the visible tree.
       - To preserve cursor: walk parentUuid chain from the captured id up to root, collecting ancestor uuids. For each, compute its <jsonl>#<line_no> id (via by_uuid). Chain ctx.expand(root).then(expand(level1)).then(... .then(cursor_to(target))) so each ancestor is in the cache by the time the next expand runs. Falls back to best-effort cursor_to if any step fails.

    3. Cursor-on-open / drill-in:
       - On main(): after constructing the Browser, if --session/--pid/--file targets a .jsonl, queue expand(jsonl).then(cursor_to(<last_voice_id>)).
       - When the user manually drills into a session (Right), the framework calls get_children; in tree mode the cursor doesn't auto-jump to last voice on drill-in unless we explicitly do so. Decision: add an 'on first time scoping or expanding a session in tree mode' jump. Simplest impl: in main(), the same cursor_to-last-voice runs once for the initial scope; further drill-ins use natural cursor (top of list). This matches user request 'On open' rather than 'every Right'.

    Last voice id resolution:
    - _scan_tree the session.
    - Walk records in REVERSE file order, return the first record where _is_voice(record) is True.
    - Compute its id <jsonl>#<n>.

    Unit tests (a couple of pure-function ones for last-voice picker), UI tests in #302.

* ## Ticket: browse-claude: voice-only filter (`h` toggle) {#340}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-16 11:38:49 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-16 11:56:01 UTC

  Add a recipe-level filter that hides non-conversational records in
  both flat and tree modes, controlled by `h` hotkey and
  `--show-all`/`--no-show-all` CLI flag. Subagent umbrellas always
  shown. Relies entirely on the framework's `Item.hidden` / `mod` op
  primitives — no destructive removes, framework handles cursor
  displacement.

  Spec: `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-16-browse-claude-voice-only-filter-design.md`

  * ## Ticket: Task: CLI flag + module global {#341}

    global at startup from `not args.show_all`.

  * ## Ticket: Task: `_passes_filter(item_id, td)` predicate {#342}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-16 11:38:49 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-16 11:41:19 UTC

    Add a helper that computes the predicate on demand:
    - voice-leaf (`<path>#<n>`): `_is_voice(td.records[n])`
    - `#prompt:N`: True
    - `#tool:N`: `_is_voice(td.records[N])`
    - `#span:N`: `any(_is_voice(r) for r in td.span_records.get(N, []))`
    - `#agent:...`: True
    Returns True unconditionally when `_FILTER_VOICE_ONLY` is False.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Item builders set `hidden` {#343}

    on `_FILTER_VOICE_ONLY and not _passes_filter(...)`. Touched:
    `_tree_item`, `_prompt_umbrella_item`, `_tool_umbrella_item`,
    `_span_umbrella_item`, `_subagent_pseudo_item` (always
    `hidden=False`), and the flat-mode message builder inside
    `_list_messages`. Listers themselves return all items —
    framework drops hidden subtrees at render time.

* ## Ticket: Interactive filter: `&` key with stacking semantics {#365}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-17 03:40:43 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-17 04:25:04 UTC

  Implements the filter design from
  `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-17-filter-design.md`. New `&`
  keybinding opens a filter prompt; live-as-you-type narrows the
  visible tree using match-promotes-ancestors semantics; Enter
  commits and stacks; Ctrl-X / Enter-on-empty clears.

  Composes with the existing `Item.hidden` flag (independent layer)
  and reuses `_apply_hide_displacement` + WYSIWYG select-all.

  * ## Ticket: Mode enum: replace `_search_mode: bool` with three-way `Mode` {#366}

    and `state._filter_active`. Optimistic for un-cached `has_children`

    empty filter, single filter, deep match scaffolding, AND of
    multiple filters, optimistic pending children.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Browser state + thread-safe API {#369}

        status: done

    Add `Browser._filters: list[str] = []`. Add thread-safe methods:
    `set_filters`, `add_filter`, `clear_filters`, and `filters` property
    (returns non-empty entries including live). All mutations go
    through `self.post(_do)` and fire `_recompute_filter_hidden`.
    Mutating writes that land during FILTER_EDIT force `_mode = NORMAL`
    (drop placeholder). Unit tests for read semantics (live entry
    surfaces, empty placeholder doesn't), write semantics (mode reset).
